tail      02:23 [observation] implementation/replay-swap-was-per-vertex: MAJOR pre-existing engine bug found by the receipt-change adversarial review (not caused by the diff — the lens question 'can receive_receipt run with a store attached during replay?' surfaced it): Vertex.replay swapped only the ROOT's _store to None, so parent replay forwarded historical facts to nested children whose stores were still attached — a stored child re-appended the parent's ENTIRE history on every load (1→2→3 rows per replay, reproduced empirically by the verify agent). Same discipline hole: no try/finally on the swap, so a raising fold mid-replay left _store=None permanently (close() silent no-op, handle leaked, boundaries dead). Fixed fdda675: _replay_guard context manager makes the swap per-TREE (walks _children recursively, saves/restores store+replaying flags in finally). Side effect worth knowing: child boundaries no longer fire mid-replay — matches replay's own documented contract ('without re-appending or firing boundaries') and prevents double-folding; the old behavior was the bug wearing a feature's shape. CALIBRATION: my own pre-check read replay() and concluded 'clean — every path nulls _store before replaying'; TRUE per-vertex, FALSE per-tree. I verified the discipline at the wrong scope. The structural sensor (workflow lens + empirical repro) caught what my targeted read did not — the read confirmed the claim I brought to it.
mid       02:23 [friction] engine-write-path-no-receipt-no-close: RESOLVED fdda675, same-day round trip: filed this morning from reading tasked's substrate as a requirements doc, landed tonight. Receipt(fact_id, tick, stored) frozen in engine; Vertex.receive_receipt is the one implementation with receive() as its tick projection (chosen over flipping Vertex.receive's return: 322 call sites, and dozens of 'if tick is not None' truthiness checks would break SILENTLY on an always-truthy Receipt — the caller sweep found this before design, not after). VertexProgram.receive returns the Receipt; close() + context managers both layers. Both consumers simplified: cmd_emit drops pre-mint and honors receipt.stored (gate-refusals now 'refused:' rc=2, was 'stored: @ None' rc=0 with zero facts written); tasked Store.emit is now 'with load_vertex_program(...): return program.receive(fact)' and its local Receipt class deleted in favor of the engine's. The stored=False trichotomy fix matters beyond ergonomics: pre-minting FABRICATED write identity for rejected facts — the receipt now originates at the append site, so it cannot lie.

mid       01:40 [friction] merge-preflight-dirt-check-path-blind: Dogfooding fix/delta-emits, escalation 2: squash_merge refuses to ff a checked-out base when the checkout has ANY uncommitted changes — but the dirt here (.serena/ deletions, unrelated WIP) does not intersect the merge paths, and git's own merge --ff-only handles non-overlapping dirt fine. Why: blanket cleanliness is the conservative read of 'never rewrite a working tree', but it conflates 'would be rewritten' with 'exists'. Fix-shape: intersect dirty paths with the squash's changed paths and only block on overlap (or attempt ff-only and surface git's own refusal). high      00:16 [friction] no-daemon-shaped-store-access: ticked (loops-tasks) runs a 2s-poll daemon over a vertex, but every engine touchpoint is CLI-shaped: load_vertex_program does KDL parse + pin-verify + compile + FULL-history replay per emit, and vertex_read replays per read. mid       05:11 [friction] no-conditional-emit: Entity-upsert consumers need a conditional emit (CAS): ticked's runner reaps dead workers by upserting work status=finished outcome=error, but between its fold read and the emit the worker may emit finished/replied — the later error upsert wins unconditionally. ticked shrinks the window by re-reading the run immediately before reaping, but a real fix is engine-level: receive(fact, expect={field: value}) that refuses when the current folded value diverges (same shape as SqliteStore.absorb_edit's expected_head CAS). Second consumer-driven case after vouch for transactional-ish semantics.

mid       22:40 [decision] architecture/param-secrets-indirection: Template params keep their declaration-state boundary (they define what a source IS), but gain opt-in env indirection: a whole-value $NAME param resolves from the process environment at compile time (engine._resolve_param_indirection); the declared $NAME form is what enters immutable genesis/edit payloads, never the resolved value. $$ escapes a literal leading $; partial interpolation unsupported (compose via separate params); missing env var fails loud at load. Literal params remain permanent declaration state — uniform rule, no secret-detection heuristic, identical posture to the env decision. Strict-tier refusal of literals (fork option A) stays deferred as policy, exactly as decision:architecture/env-values-are-ingress deferred it. This closes the one question that survived the internal-table CLOSE. Landed f4eb863 with regression tests incl. payload-retains-declared-form lock-in.

mid       16:18 [decision] architecture/env-values-are-ingress: Env VALUES in source declarations are INGRESS (SPEC §9.5 secrets-indirection), not declaration state — payloads record only the key set; values live in the .vertex file and are re-attached at resolution exactly like the store locator. Consequences: secrets (and all literals — uniform rule, no secret-detection heuristic) never enter genesis/edit payloads, dumps, or transit; a value edit is live without ceremony; a key-set edit is a real declaration diff surfaced at absorb -n. The A/B fork (Kyle 2026-07-13): refusing literals at absorb (A) is a POLICY and thus strict's domain — deferred as a strict-tier candidate (strict vertex could force $VAR indirection so secrets never touch the committed file either); B is the representation-level substrate rule and ships now. Boundary held: template params stay declaration state (they define what a source IS); env is execution environment. Referenced .loop content is hash-pinned (content_sha256) in source-defined payloads for drift detectability; portable resolved-source capture deferred to a loop-document-form slice (raw text would re-leak env).

high      04:41 [design] architecture/batch-emit-ingress: Batch emit as first-class ingress — consolidates three 2026-07-03 frictions (N=1 speculative then, consumer-demanded now: Sol's homelab audit did 88 emit invocations, one process per fact, and cited all three by name). Proposed shape: (1) sl emit <vertex> --ndjson <file|-> — the batch surface speaks the SAME fact-per-line grammar sync sources already emit (probes→loops sync); this is exposure of an existing primitive, not a new one (dissolution). (2) Symbolic intra-batch IDs: a line may declare id=$sym and later lines ref=$sym; the batch resolves forward refs topologically before append, so strict typed-edge graphs are authorable without manual ordering — and the batch file itself becomes a replayable build manifest (Sol's missing-import-manifest finding). (3) Atomic: one batch = one transaction with per-batch receipt (precedent: absorb_edit all-or-nothing posture); strict-mode validation runs across the whole batch pre-append so a mid-batch refusal leaves nothing half-written. (4) Degenerate single-emit ergonomics ride along: message=- (stdin) and message=@file fall out of the same reader — subsumes friction/stdin-message-for-emit. Scope cut: seal-fanout folds in ONLY its authoring half (a batch is one authored act, closable by one boundary); the cross-store simultaneity half stays with thread:workspace-linked-cuts (a new claim needing its own primitive). Open: whether quick-capture (sl note — store now, categorize at sweep) is a batch-ingress degenerate case or its own verb; lean own-verb-later, it's a capture-latency problem not a bulk problem.

tail      22:38 [friction] seal-provenance-not-passed-to-lenses: Refuse-to-guess violation found by the homelab-audit consumer (2026-07-12): loops store verify reports 694/694 facts sealed on the audit store, while ordinary terminal reads render "Live unsealed fold" — because the lens receives projection=None and the render path interprets MISSING cut provenance as a POSITIVE claim of unsealed-ness. Same errors-as-state discipline as everywhere else: absence of evidence rendered as evidence of absence is a lie wearing the costume of a status line. Note the fix has two layers: (a) substrate — thread cut provenance through the read path into render_context; (b) render honesty — never default a provenance-bearing banner from None.

mid       04:05 [decision] design/absorb-genesis-atomic-primitive: S1 review round (Codex on eaa8297: 2 TOCTOU blockers) forced the ceremony's core into an engine primitive: SqliteStore.absorb_genesis — genesis-exists check, era-pin reads (chain head + fact cursor), payload assembly, signing, and append all inside ONE BEGIN IMMEDIATE transaction. Kills both races (pin falsified by concurrent emit; double-mint by concurrent absorbs) and the probe-vs-actual signing gap (signature checked over the final payload before commit, rollback if absent). Two deliberate non-obviousnesses: (1) NO unique index on the genesis kind — merge legitimately carries FOREIGN genesis rows as inert citizens (lineage carriage), so uniqueness is transaction-scoped logic, never schema; (2) refuse-if-ANY-genesis is provisionally conservative — pre-S6 a store cannot distinguish self from merged-foreign genesis (that distinction arrives with _decl.merged receipts); revisit at S6. The primitive is protocol surface loops-go mirrors — its contract is the §9.2 era-opening made operational. Reservation also deepened to engine ingest tier (Vertex.receive refuses _decl.*), .loop validation, route keys, _run_close.

tail      23:47 [decision] design/declaration-document-subjects-and-order: S0 review round (Codex gpt-5.6-sol on f82e9e3: 1 blocker, 5 majors — all confirmed) forced two protocol calls on the document form. (1) SOURCE SUBJECTS: human-meaningful base (template path / bare path / command) + deterministic collision suffix in encounter order (base, base#2, base#3) — reorders of distinct sources stay stable, duplicates disambiguate deterministically; picked over content-hash subjects (edit=retire+define churn) and pure ordinals (reorder=spurious redefinition of every subject). (2) ORDER IS MEANING: every multi-instance document payload (kind-defined, source-defined, member-defined, observer-defined, lens-defined) carries integer order=; projection sorts by (order, subject). Rationale: sequential source blocks, boundary match order, and kind declaration order (salience rendering) are all meaning the per-subject Latest fold would otherwise destroy; a reorder edit re-emitting affected subjects is honest because order is meaning where declared. Also enforced at serialization: float finiteness + recursive JSON-safety (str keys, JSON values) — JCS canonicalization must never be the first thing to notice. Empty-present vs None collections: preserve via vertex-defined presence markers where loader-reachable (empty sources block IS: loader.py:595), else normalize+document.
mid       23:32 [decision] design/absorb-ceremony-verb: RATIFIED (Kyle 2026-07-11): the declaration-absorption ceremony is 'sl store absorb <vertex>' — rides the existing store ceremony group (verify/rebirth/reanchor precedent). One verb, two eras: first invocation on a store = genesis/era-opening (parse .vertex once, emit signed _decl.genesis with whole document + protocol version, pinning chain head + fact cursor); subsequent invocations = S4 edit re-absorb (diff at subject granularity, changed subjects re-emit whole document + change= annotation). Top-level 'sl absorb' rejected: seal/close earn top-level by frequency, absorb is once-per-store + occasional edits. Split verbs (store genesis / store absorb) rejected: two verbs for one mechanism fails dissolution unless ceremonies genuinely diverge. Future pairing: 'sl store render' for KDL materialization from fold head (S4, may defer).

tail      20:00 [design] rendering/status-aware-kind-budget: Mechanism for a query-keyed default budget that hides terminal-status rows from a kind's default fold view -- the concrete first application of plan:curation-in-surface Open Decision B, scoped to friction by design/practice/friction-kind-lifecycle's corpus finding that friction's default view surfaces high-salience resolved items above open ones (the triggering observation: emit-receipt-on-write, resolved, sitting at the top of the default friction view).  Shape:  1. Declaration -- a new kind-level clause in .vertex KDL, sibling to fold/preview/search/edge: `hide status="resolved"` (multi-value: `hide status="resolved,parked"` if ever needed). Parsed by libs/lang/loader.py alongside the existing kind-block clauses.  2. Mechanism -- surface.py budget() gains a `hide` param (same shape as the existing salience_window param): filters rows whose payload[status_field] matches the hidden set, sets Window.limited_by="status", records a count. Pure transform, same pattern as limit/last/salience_window.  3. Scope -- FOLD VIEW ONLY (current-state default read). --facts (event/lifecycle history) stays faithful always -- different read axis, and corpus audits (this session's friction audit ran on --facts + --json to verify status transitions) need the untouched history regardless of what the fold view curates.  4. Uniform across encoders -- the hide runs in the Surface budget stage, before text and --json rendering diverge, so both channels see the identical cut (satisfies the invariance constraint Decision B already proved: query-keyed is allowed, channel-keyed is not).  5. Defeat -- --all shows everything (reusing the vocabulary docs/dev/umwelt-divergence-and-curation-in-surface-2026-06-28.md already picked for in-band windowing defeat, one vocabulary for all budget-cuts). An explicit status= predicate in the same read auto-disables the default hide for that read (asking for status=resolved while hiding resolved would be incoherent).  6. Provenance -- Window gets an honest limited_by="status" + shown/total counts, same no-silent-caps discipline as every other budget cut.  First concrete instance: friction { hide status="resolved" } in .loops/project.vertex, once implemented.  Touches: libs/lang/loader.py (grammar), apps/loops/src/loops/surface.py (budget()), apps/loops/src/loops/cli/operation.py + dispatch.py (wiring), .loops/project.vertex (declaration), tests. mid       05:13 [friction] fts-search-declaration-not-retroactive: [ref correction only, message unchanged] Declaring a new 'search' field on a kind in a .vertex file does NOT retroactively index that kind's existing facts. _ensure_fts (vertex_reader.py) advances fts_state.last_rowid monotonically and skips kinds without a search declaration AT THE TIME their rowid is scanned -- once last_rowid passes a fact, it is never re-considered even if search gets declared for its kind later. Hit live 2026-07-11: adding search to decision/thread/task/plan/session/log/cite/hypothesis/friction/observation/seal in .loops/project.vertex (previously only 'design' declared search) left --match returning 0 results on 2948 pre-existing facts until facts_fts + fts_state were manually dropped to force a full rebuild. Contrast with typed-edges, which is genuinely retroactive because it's a read-time overlay, not a write-time indexing cursor -- the FTS mechanism looks like the same kind of late-bound declaration but silently is not. No 'sl store reindex' verb exists to do this safely/discoverably (had to hand-drop tables via sqlite3 directly). Fix-shape: (a) a 'sl store reindex <vertex>' verb that drops+rebuilds facts_fts/fts_state (small, matches the add-verb-gap-boundary-and-preview pattern -- machinery exists, just no CLI surface); (b) at minimum, Window.unindexed or a receipt-time WARN should flag 'this kind now declares search but has N pre-declaration facts not yet indexed' so the gap is visible instead of silently returning zero matches. Every vertex that adds a search declaration to an already-populated kind hits this.

tail      04:50 [design] architecture/ephemeral-topology-with-flag: A --with flag, general across vertex ops (read/emit/fold/cite), that supplies an ephemeral topology root for cross-store ref resolution without persisting a named aggregation vertex first. Closes the inversion in architecture/combinatorial-vertices (2026-03-01, never built): that decision said 'temporary by default, persisted if the pattern proves useful' but everything built since (cli-completion, loops add <vertex> combine) is the persisted half only -- there is no ephemeral half. Mechanism: reuses the existing topology-roots resolution machinery (_topology_roots_for_emit for write, the combine-walk for read) -- --with just feeds it an extra root that isn't discovered from a .vertex file. Two open design questions before implementation: (1) argument shape -- --with <name> (resolve_vertex lookup) vs --with </path/to/.vertex> (raw path, matching combine's own vertex entries) vs both; (2) whether a promotion convenience (turn a --with pairing that keeps recurring into a persisted loops add combine) is worth building alongside, or whether the existing manual add combine command is already sufficient and coupling them is premature.

high      02:48 [thread] fidelity-contract-tests: M3 loops-adoption-spike evidence-gathering COMPLETE (audit-only, no code changed). Nine facts recorded. SIGNATURE VERDICT: (data, fidelity, width) IS sufficient for the static render contract — semantic_article's decomposed visible/chars/lines vote holds across all 25+ lenses (they collapse exactly into painted Fidelity fields, per lens-signature-tiers + call-lens-fidelity-teardown-adapter which shows loops already builds a Fidelity then tears it down to feed the lenses). Left status=open: the evidence is recorded but the actual deletions (dead fn, piped param, closure glue) and painted's signature choice are downstream work for painted M4 / a loops follow-up, not this audit.
mid       02:48 [observation] rendering/store-app-holds-no-fidelity-duplication: Audit item 2 named tui/store_app.py as a place a landed painted declaration grammar might let loops delete. Finding: NOTHING in store_app.py is flag-compilation or Fidelity-parsing residue — clearing a red herring from the M3 scope. The FidelityState dataclass there is a NAVIGATION state (a facts-within-a-tick-window drill cursor), a domain concept that merely shares the word fidelity; it has no relation to painted's render Fidelity. store_app imports painted's Block/Surface/views (data_explorer, list_view) and lays out against layout(width, height) — it is a legitimate Surface consumer, not a shadow renderer. So the deletable duplication surfaced by this spike lives entirely in cli/fidelity.py (dead fidelity_from_args) and the run_cli render-closure glue (rendering/run-cli-adapter-inventory) plus the piped re-derivation (rendering/piped-is-fabricated-tty-fact) — NOT in the TUI. Recording this so the M3 delete-list is not padded with a false target.
mid       02:47 [observation] rendering/call-lens-fidelity-teardown-adapter: A second, subtler adapter loops hand-builds around painted's render contract: the Fidelity TEARDOWN. loops resolves a proper painted Fidelity upstream (op.fidelity, built via parse_fidelity) but its lenses do NOT accept a Fidelity — they accept (data, zoom, width, *, visible, chars, lines, ...). So dispatch.py + lens_resolver.call_lens tear the Fidelity back apart: _zoom_of(fidelity) extracts fidelity.depth as a Zoom, then visible/chars/lines are spread as loose kwargs via extra.setdefault(...). call_lens then inspects each lens signature and forwards only the kwargs whose names match (or all, for **kwargs lenses). This is a build-up-then-tear-down round trip: painted's parse_fidelity assembles a Fidelity, loops immediately decomposes it into (zoom, visible, chars, lines) to feed lenses written before Fidelity existed. Under semantic_article's vote the fix is to have lenses take fidelity DIRECTLY as the second arg — then _zoom_of, the visible/chars/lines setdefault dance, and call_lens's whole kwarg-forwarding inspection machinery all dissolve. This is the strongest single piece of evidence FOR the decomposed-kwargs-into-one-Fidelity-object direction: loops already has the object and is paying to un-build it at every render.
mid       02:47 [observation] rendering/run-cli-adapter-inventory: M3 ask: record every adapter loops hand-builds to reuse a painted renderer through run_cli. loops has TWO dispatch spines and both hand-build glue. SPINE 1 legacy run_cli path — commands/ still call painted.run_cli(fetch=, render=) directly; each supplies a render(ctx, data) closure that is pure adapter boilerplate translating painted's CliContext into a loops lens call. Inventory of the render closures: ls.py:204 (declarations_view) and :518 (kind_stat_view); population.py:81 (vertices_view); store.py:654 (tick_chain_view), :723 (stats_view), :788 (store_view); ticks.py:103 and stream.py:77 (resolve-then-call composition adapters); sync.py:170 and :321 (sync_view); devtools.py x4. The recurring glue is exactly: 'w = ctx.width if ctx.is_tty else None; return LENS(data, ctx.zoom, w, piped=not ctx.is_tty)'. Every one re-derives width-from-TTY and piped-from-TTY by hand. SPINE 2 new siftd-shape path — cli/dispatch.py:dispatch owns the same branches natively (action/interactive/live/static) and no longer routes static through run_cli; it computes width from sys.stdout.isatty() itself. DISSOLUTION: under a (data, fidelity, width) renderer contract where painted owns the fetch->render->emit loop and passes width already normalized (None=piped), every Spine-1 render closure collapses to nothing — the ctx.zoom/ctx.width/ctx.is_tty unpacking and the piped re-derivation are the whole adapter, and all of it is painted re-exposing what painted already knows. The closures exist only because loops re-reads TTY state painted computed one frame earlier.
mid       02:47 [observation] rendering/siftd-mirror-has-drifted: Side-by-side of the two claimed-mirror fidelity_from_args implementations (loops cli/fidelity.py vs siftd src/siftd/cli/_common.py). They are NOT identical in logic — the Mirrors siftd docstring is aspirational, and the shadow copies have DRIFTED. Divergences: (1) DEPTH FLAGS — loops reads -q/--quiet (depth 0) and -v/--verbose count (1 to depth 2, 2+ to depth 3), default_depth 1; siftd reads --brief (depth 0) and --full (depth 3) booleans, default 1. Different flag vocabulary AND different arity (count vs bool). (2) VISIBLE DERIVATION — loops is PARAMETERIZED: caller passes a visible={flag_attr: tag_name} mapping and any truthy/int>0 flag lights its tag; siftd HARDCODES its domain tags: seeds {text}, adds thinking on --thinking/--full, adds tools on --tools/--full. (3) BUDGET — loops takes explicit --max-chars AND --max-lines (two axes); siftd takes --chars plus a --brief=>80 shortcut and has NO lines axis. (4) default_chars vs default_depth parameter surface differs. SIGNIFICANCE for M3: the drift is not sloppiness — it is EVIDENCE that the flag-to-facet vocabulary is genuinely per-consumer (loops disclosure axes are facts/refs over threads/decisions; siftd's are text/thinking/tools over transcripts). Two independently-drifting hand-copies of the same SHAPE is precisely the signal that argues for a painted DECLARATION grammar (each consumer declares its flag->facet map, painted compiles it) over a shared parsing function — a shared function would have to absorb both vocabularies and cannot.
mid       02:47 [decision] rendering/fidelity-from-args-is-dead-shadow-copy: Headline M3 duplication finding. apps/loops/src/loops/cli/fidelity.py:fidelity_from_args — the function whose docstring claims it Mirrors siftd cli/_common.py and which the thread named as the general-purpose Fidelity parsing loops should not own — has ZERO live callers. grep across all of apps/loops (src + tests) finds no reference outside its own definition file. The LIVE fidelity-compilation path is cli/views/fold.py:~515, which already delegates the pure-terminal axes to painted's OWN painted.cli.types.parse_fidelity(args, parse_zoom(args)) and then overlays only the two domain-query selectors (facts, refs>0) via a dataclasses.replace on visible. So loops ALREADY does not own general Fidelity parsing on its hot path — painted's parse_fidelity does it. fidelity_from_args is pure dead residue of the pre-painted-parse_fidelity design. RECOMMENDATION (audit-only, not executed here): fidelity_from_args is deletable TODAY, independent of any new painted declaration grammar — the grammar it was compensating for already landed as parse_fidelity. Deleting it satisfies M3's 'loops owns no duplicate general-purpose Fidelity parsing' exit criterion outright. The only thing painted's FUTURE declaration grammar would additionally absorb is the small domain-visible overlay (the if args.facts add facts / if refs add refs block in fold.py), which is the legitimate app-side facet mapping, not general parsing.
mid       02:47 [observation] rendering/height-offered-only-in-tui: M3 asks: record where height is OFFERED to a renderer vs merely KNOWN by the caller. Findings across both loops render paths. STATIC CLI path (dispatch.py + every run_cli render closure): only WIDTH is offered — dispatch computes width from shutil.get_terminal_size().columns (or None when piped) and passes it as the third positional; height is available to the caller (get_terminal_size().lines exists, ctx carries it) but is NEVER passed to any static lens. So in the static path height is merely KNOWN, never OFFERED. TUI/Surface path (tui/store_app.py, tui/autoresearch_app.py): height IS offered — the Surface calls layout(self, width, height) and the app stores both self._w and self._h and lays out against the viewport height. CONCLUSION for the signature question: a static (data, fidelity, width) signature that omits height matches actual static-path usage exactly (height is never wanted there); height is a live/Surface concern, which is consistent with painted keeping offered-allocation in the Surface tier rather than the static renderer signature. No static loops lens is starved by a height-free signature.
mid       02:46 [observation] rendering/piped-is-fabricated-tty-fact: M3 exit criterion says loops semantic renderers must require no fabricated mode, TTY, or stream facts. loops VIOLATES this via one fact: piped. It is computed as (not ctx.is_tty) or (not sys.stdout.isatty()) and threaded as a keyword into ~11 lens entrypoints: declarations_view, kind_stat_view, vertices_view, store_view, tick_chain_view, stats_view, ticks_view, stream_view, confluence_view, horizon_view, graph_view, and the built-in fold_view. It is REDUNDANT: width already carries the same two-state contract (concrete int on a TTY, None when piped) — normalize_width and its docstring in lens_resolver.py state this explicitly, and every run_cli render closure sets width via 'w = ctx.width if ctx.is_tty else None' right beside 'piped=not ctx.is_tty'. So the same TTY bit is encoded TWICE at every call site, once as width=None and once as piped=True. Dissolution: lenses that branch on piped can branch on 'width is None' instead; piped as a param disappears and the fabricated-TTY-fact criterion is met with zero new painted machinery. This is deletable independently of the declaration grammar.
mid       02:46 [observation] rendering/fold-view-maximal-signature: The built-in apps/loops/src/loops/lenses/fold.py fold_view is the UNION signature — the everything-lens that proves what a general loops renderer actually consumes: (data, zoom, width, *, vertex_name, vertex_path, visible, lines, chars, piped). Decompose those kwargs into three categories and the M3 signature answer falls out cleanly: (1) visible/chars/lines = painted Fidelity axes (fold_view even rebuilds a Fidelity from zoom+these inside semantic_article) — these BELONG in the fidelity arg; (2) vertex_name/vertex_path = domain identity, an app-specific valued facet, render-irrelevant — belongs OUTSIDE painted, bound by the app via closure or an app-context, matching the roadmap's 'keep app-specific facets outside painted' constraint; (3) piped = a fabricated TTY fact that duplicates width's None-sentinel (see rendering/piped-is-fabricated-tty-fact). So (data, fidelity, width) is sufficient for the RENDER contract once piped dissolves and domain identity is bound app-side rather than passed as a render param.
mid       02:46 [observation] rendering/lens-signature-tiers: M3 signature-sufficiency evidence. Enumerated all 25+ loops lens entrypoints beyond semantic_article. They fall in THREE tiers against semantic_article's (data, zoom, width, *, visible, chars, lines) vote. TIER A pure (data, zoom, width) -> Block, no extra kwargs: compile_view, run_facts_view, run_ticks_view, test_view, validate_view, sync_view, pop_view. TIER B needs a piped bool (TTY register split) sometimes plus palette/vertex_name: confluence_view, horizon_view, graph_view, store_view (+palette), declarations_view/_render_stat_view/kind_stat_view, vertices_view, stream_view (+vertex_name), ticks_view, tick_chain_view, stats_view. TIER C needs the Fidelity budget axes visible/chars/lines: semantic_article.fold_view (the vote, explicit), plus **kwargs absorbers deliberation.fold_view, reconcile.fold_view, session_landing.fold_view. VERDICT: the semantic_article vote (decomposed visible/chars/lines) holds — those three collapse exactly into a painted Fidelity's fields, so (data, fidelity, width) subsumes every Tier A and Tier C signature. It does NOT subsume the two EXTRA kinds of thing Tier B threads: a TTY fact (piped) and domain identity (vertex_name/vertex_path/palette). Those are the real signature question, detailed in sibling observations.

high      00:39 [decision] design/horizon-unarmed-rollup: AMENDED (Kyle 2026-07-05, build-review ruling): unarmed = uncovered by ANY declared trigger, not merely 'no own boundary'. A vertex-level boundary's tick sweeps the entire window across all kinds, so every loop under it is COVERED — bounded accumulation, not silent; such loops never enter the ◦ roster (the armed vertex row already carries their window). The builder's loop-granularity reading (no per-loop tick series ⇒ unarmed) was rejected: it would render project's every kind as '◦ never ticks' while the seal boundary ticks them each session close, double-reporting the armed unsealed count with a contradicting story and recreating the census noise this decision exists to avoid. Consequence: the unarmed segment appears only on vertices with zero vertex-level boundaries — exactly the silent-accumulation case Design named.

tail      22:36 [observation] rendering/flags-words-edges-arrows: Register idiom generalized from the P4 review: symbols split into FLAGS (a judgment/status the pipe consumer can't reconstruct — degrade to words: tier ◆→high, horizon ▲→approaching) vs EDGE NOTATION (←/→ ARE the notation, no better word exists, pipe already speaks → in every chain path — arrows survive both registers). What looked inconsistency-shaped (arrows survived the pipe after ▲ didn't) is a rule the next lens can follow. Documented in _grammar module docstring.
mid       22:36 [decision] design/rollup-shed-only-what-degrades: The -q rollup grammar rule reconciling graph's wrap with confluence's shed: shed ONLY what degrades gracefully; wrap what can't. A rollup part may sit after shed_from iff its information survives shedding in degraded form elsewhere on the line (confluence top names shed because the observer count carries +N). A part with no degraded form (graph's top hub — dropping it loses the fact entirely while the pipe carries it) never sheds; the caller wraps the logical line via wrap_hanging. AMENDS the canonical-MINIMAL-one-liner framing: 'one-liner' means one LOGICAL line — narrow TTYs may wrap, never silently drop what the pipe carries. Companion register-idiom rule documented in _grammar module docstring: FLAGS are words on the pipe (tier→high, ▲→approaching), EDGE NOTATION is arrows (←/→ survive both registers — direction has no better word, the pipe already speaks → in chains).

mid       19:24 [decision] design/graph-build1-scope: AMENDED at build: chain depth cap 32 -> 128. Build finding: with memoized DFS, a cap below real chain length (live chains reach ~60) memo-poisons — nodes first reached past the cap memoize truncated paths, making 'longest' order-dependent. The cycle guard alone guarantees termination; the cap is purely a Python-recursion safety valve, so it must sit ABOVE realistic chain depth, not act as a result bound. Shipped in graph build-1.
tail      19:04 [decision] design/strata-cut-ratified: Strata CUT from 0.6.0 RATIFIED (autonomous-run assessment, executing the designated cut from 060-view-sequence). Grounds beyond cost: cascade lineage is NOT key-joinable — _tick_to_fact (vertex.py:911-927) carries child tick payload/observer/origin onto the parent fact but NEVER the child tick id/since/window_hash, so read-side tree assembly is a heuristic ts+payload reconciliation (ambiguous on identical payloads, unprovable) requiring N cross-store opens + recursive assembly + a new fetch shape. A view rendering heuristic lineage as if it were attested structure fails the static-honest bar on PRINCIPLE — this is the rewind-honesty argument (SPEC 9.3) applied to Strata. Consequence fed forward: the 0.7.0 internal table (SPEC 9) should carry parent_tick_id / child_vertex_ref on tick rows, turning Strata into a straight recursive query over stored FKs. Strata rides 0.7.0.

mid       05:39 [observation] paradigm/capture-cheap-assert-later-read-retroactive: Three independent designs converged on one pattern: typed edges (address-field -> declared edge), observer typing (bare string -> declared Peer), delegation (slash-path -> vouched relation). General form: capture is cheap/declaration-free at emit time; structure is asserted later and lights up retroactively at read time (schema-on-read); the store never blocks on ontology; each read surface advertises its own promotion candidates (reconcile -> edge declarations, Confluence -> peer declarations / unendorsed compounds). This is a paradigm property, not three coincidences.
mid       05:39 [decision] design/observer-compound-delegation-path: RATIFIED (Kyle 2026-07-04): 'a/b' observer names read as delegation paths FOR GROUPING ONLY. Confluence nests compounds under their root and rolls the root gutter tier up MAX-over-descendants, but claims no edge — a name-parse has the same epistemic status as an undeclared address-field. When vouch ships endorsement assertions, the read layer joins both: asserted relations render as edges; slash-compounds without a backing assertion render as implied/unendorsed. The slash form is the degenerate inline encoding of the same relation, never migrated away; the gap between implied and endorsed is itself the signal.
untiered  04:59 [cite] late-bound retroactive declaration precedent grounds observer-typing-dissolves-to-declared-peer
mid       04:58 [decision] design/observer-typing-dissolves-to-declared-peer: RATIFIED (Kyle 2026-07-04): no observer-type enum. Observer is the base level — a bare string. 'Type' = whether the name resolves to a declared Peer and what that declaration says (horizon/potential; attested-vs-bare derivable from signing). Declaration is late-bound + retroactive per the typed-edges precedent: a peer declaration lights up historical facts by that observer at read time, no re-emit; undeclared observers stay inert bare strings. Confluence build-1 renders undeclared observers bare; declaration is the upgrade path — Confluence surfaces peer-declaration candidates the way reconcile surfaces edge-declaration candidates (read surface generates demand for the dormant Peer primitive, read-only, before Digest needs it for gating).

mid       21:20 [decision] architecture/replay-fold-only-cascade: Replay is fold-only end to end: receive() guards store-append on _replaying and replay-forwards only to STORELESS children with replay-mode propagated recursively; store-owning children replay from their OWN stores (facts landed there live at receive time — re-routing parent history duplicates). A storeless discover root now replays its store-owning members (previously returned 0 and skipped them). Fixes friction:discover-root-replay-cascade-duplication; fix/discover-cascade c2643dd.

mid       19:25 [friction] discover-root-replay-cascade-duplication: Giving a discover root its own store is a landmine: Vertex.receive appends routed facts into child stores (vertex.py:391) and replay() re-routes root facts to children with the child NOT in replay mode, so every program load duplicates facts into member stores and re-mints child ticks. Observed live in gruel.network (relay.db 98->106 facts, 3->7 ticks from probes; recovered via git checkout of the committed dbs). Two engine fixes landed while diagnosing: materialize_vertex now skips children whose store path is unreachable on this host (OSError -> skip, monitor.vertex case) and passes tick_signer/fact_signer down to children so cascaded mints in signed-era stores do not get refused. Remaining: replay must propagate replay-mode to children (no store-append, no tick mint), and the design question of whether discover children should be cascade targets at all vs read-only aggregation.
high      19:25 [friction] seal-fanout-across-workspace-stores: A workspace with several sibling stores (gruel.network: relay + homelab-coord + project) needs N separate seals at session wrap. Wanted: a root-level single-seal verb (e.g. sl seal --all on a discover root) that walks member stores and ticks each one with an open window. The cascade half-exists: a root vertex with store+discover routes a root seal fact into children and fires their boundaries — but that path is unsound today (see friction:discover-root-replay-cascade-duplication), so fan-out must be a deliberate feature, not the accidental hybrid.

mid       18:56 [friction] no-bulk-emit-for-interactive-use: Migrating ~60 memory docs = ~60 separate sl emit invocations, each a full CLI round-trip with a giant quoted message body. Sync sources already speak ndjson (probes emit fact-per-line consumed by loops sync) but there's no interactive equivalent: sl emit --ndjson <file> (or stdin stream) accepting the same shape would have made the migration one command per batch and makes any future bulk ingestion (changelog-as-facts conversion, another repo's memory migration) tractable. Same primitive the sync engine has — expose it on the emit surface.
tail      18:56 [friction] fold-key-mistakes-leave-orphan-sediment: Fold keys are per-vertex per-kind (topic= vs name= vs agent=) and must be known BEFORE emit; the WARN receipt names the expected key (good) but only after storing an orphaned <no-fold> fact. Hit 3x in one day migrating gruel.network memories: decision name= vs topic=, then 6 relationship facts with name= vs agent= — 7 orphan facts now permanent sediment beside their corrected re-emits. Fix-shapes: (a) interactive emits could default strict (reject, don't store, when fold key missing — strict mode exists but isn't default); (b) an emit preflight that echoes the kind's fold shape; (c) orphan-fact cleanup story (compact that drops <no-fold>? explicit tombstone?). The receipt catches the mistake; the substrate still keeps the wreckage.
mid       18:56 [friction] emit-friction-exceeds-file-write: Post memory->store migration in gruel.network (2026-07-03), emit is the SLOWER capture path vs the zero-thought file-write it replaced: an emit demands kind choice, per-vertex fold key, ref selection, and shell-quoting of long prose bodies — a memory file demanded none of these. The structure is the value, but the marginal capture cost risks under-emission under time pressure, which is the failure mode that kills accumulation systems. Fix-shapes: (a) message=- stdin / message=@file (friction/stdin-message-for-emit, still open — this is now load-bearing for an entire memory workflow, not a nicety); (b) a quick-capture verb (sl note?) that stores now and defers kind/key categorization to sweep time — matches how reroute-logs already work; (c) fold-key hints at the prompt rather than only in the post-hoc receipt. Emitting-as-memory should be the EASIER path than files were (Kyle's framing).
tail      17:23 [friction] per-section-salience-budget-missing: 0.5.0's --limit is global top-N by salience; there is no per-section (per-kind) budget in a single read. The SessionStart-context use case wants 'top-3 of each kind' — census (-q) is too little, full fold (35KB for relay) is too much, global --limit 3 collapses a 7-kind fold to 3 rows from whichever kinds dominate salience. Workaround in gruel.network hook: N reads, one per kind, concatenated. Fix-shape: --limit accepting a per-section mode (e.g. --limit 3 --by kind, mirroring --count --by), or a zoom level between census and full. Found by relay rewriting the broken hook 2026-07-03; companion to friction/breaking-cli-flag-change-broke-consumer-hooks-silently.

mid       03:34 [decision] design/tier-one-home-inheritance: G4 stream tier-inheritance fork RESOLVED: tier assignment has exactly one home — _assign_tiers over the entity projection; every other axis INHERITS, nothing re-computes. Stream path folds the vertex (compute-only, render-invisible — rendered rows stay the windowed facts), projects the entity Surface, derives tier_map(surface) -> {(kind,key): tier}; event rows inherit via key lookup. Ticks consume the SAME map with MAX aggregation (tree-cut rows). Rejected: (a) two Surfaces to the lens (pushes fold-semantics join into render layer); window-local quantiles (noise over salience=1). high      03:29 [decision] design/tier-allocated-disclosure: Fidelity = f(intent, specificity, volume). AMENDS granularity-complete-key-address: flip-invariance holds on every retrieval path (address, -v/-vv, --full, piped); the TTY default-zoom ORIENTATION view is exempt — tiers are quantile-relative, so rows may flip body/headline as the population moves, which is honest for orientation (attention moved). mid       01:07 [thread] retrospective-ticks: REFRAMED (Kyle 2026-07-02): not a wholly new primitive — 'sl seal'/'close' was ALWAYS meant to be arbitrary manual tick-drawing. Retrospective ticks = seal with its two pinned defaults relaxed: (1) TIME — seal ticks now-over-accumulated-window; these draw over any historical window or selection; (2) SCOPE — seal is one vertex; these span a store federation. Two motivating cases with different hardness: HOA board meeting (knowable window, many stores — hoa emails, neighborhood facebook, texts, feed vendor research, siftd LLM conversations, photos — drawn near-in-time; ~'seal across a federation with an explicit window', fixed boundary sensible) vs INSURANCE EVENT (relevance revealed retroactively — no attention signal existed at the time, so selection must be query-driven, not salience-trace-driven). Residence question sharpened: a cross-store tick lives in an owned event-scoped vertex (events/hoa-2026-07 shape) whose tick refs foreign facts → lands directly on the substrate arc's inert-foreign-lineages store-ops work. Attestation question stands: an after-the-fact tick is a NEW attested event referencing a historical window, never inserted into it.
mid       01:02 [thread] retrospective-ticks: New primitive surfaced (Kyle 2026-07-02): the RETROSPECTIVE TICK — draw a boundary AFTER the fact around a curated selection of facts, possibly CROSS-VERTEX, turning a reconstructed trajectory into a first-class foldable/citable period. Today's ticks are forward boundaries (declared, fire at emit time); this is selection→tick over history, spanning stores. Motivating stack: jeeves/household federation where stores funnel up via combine and one may want to tick 'that particular thread' across all of them months later. Also explains why ls/structural visibility is load-bearing: can't draw a boundary across a federation you can't see the shape of. Open questions: selection grammar (query? hand-picked ULIDs? salience-trace window?), cross-vertex tick residence, interaction with the signed tick chain (retrospective ticks in an attested chain = era question — likely relates to internal-table/genesis ceremony work).
mid       01:02 [observation] design/salience-as-attention-trace: The salience feed (Kyle 2026-07-02) reframes salience as a TRACE, not a scalar: three signal strata — ambient scrape (feeds/discords), deliberate capture (likes/'good article', incl. out-of-subscription ingestion), actual attention (browser history on top) — recording what had attention WHEN. Never about deletion. Consequences: salience-now = fold over attention events; salience-at-T = same fold over a window — the append-only store + ref-as-attention-event (UNION, accumulating) already IS the trace; the feed needs the 0.7.0 temporal cursor to query it, which is the strongest motivation yet for rewind (stronger than audit framing). Dissolution-as-coverage-not-deletion (already ratified) satisfies 'never get rid of things' as-is. Retrospection use case: reconstruct a trajectory months later ('the Shannon-Weaver rabbit hole', 'all the 3D-printing hop-skipping') across topic hops.
mid       01:02 [decision] design/salience-dials-vertex-declared: Kyle (2026-07-02): salience DIALS are VERTEX-DECLARED — the grammar owns the contract's SHAPE (three terms, four tiers, max propagation, view-invariance); the vertex declares the weights/cutoffs/lifecycle (feed dials recency up + inbound down; design vertex opposite; novel may key recency off fictional time). There is nowhere else for them to live, and the vertex-state-in-store arc makes it GOOD not just necessary: dials become historized events with provenance — 'why did the rail change' becomes a why-drill, tuning attention is itself attested. mid       00:25 [decision] design/grammar-domain-neutrality: Kyle's catch (2026-07-02, echoing the painted semantic-renderer reframing): the grammar layer must not bake THIS vertex's domain vocabulary into rendering — 'status-aware ⊘' assumed a status=open lifecycle field that is our schema, not loops'. Data-equivalent of semantic staleness exists in two layers: (1) the three-term salience contract is already domain-neutral, and digest-coverage IS data-level staleness (dissolved when covered, not when old — identical for a design thread covered by a decision and a chat memory covered by a consolidation digest); (2) interim ⊘ follows the DECLARED-semantics pattern (fold keys, typed edges): a kind declares its lifecycle field (e.g. lifecycle "status" open="open,in-progress"), late-bound + retroactive; ⊘ = aged-while-open per declaration; undeclaring stores never rail ⊘. General principle: grammar consumes declared semantics, never assumes field vocabulary. Doc §5b amended.

high      21:46 [thread] vertex-state-in-store: Dissolution completes (Kyle 2026-07-01): with the internal table implemented, the .vertex FILE is just a convenience — a file materialization (checkout) of the internal table's head state. high      21:38 [thread] vertex-state-in-store: Taxonomy for the internal table (Kyle+Fable 2026-07-01), from the framing 'the .vertex is the definition of this topology of semantic attention.' Membership test: could two readers at different TIMES disagree about the same facts because this changed? If yes, historize. Three strata all pass: (1) INTERPRETATION — kinds, fold ops, edge decls, boundary decls, search decls: what facts MEAN. (2) CONSTITUTION — combine/discover membership, peers, grants, observer registry/keys: whose facts and which stores CONSTITUTE the view. (3) ATTESTATION — ticks, seals: already historized, the precedent. Excluded by the same test: lenses and preview fields (change pixels, not fold/salience/traversal — a rewound fold under today's lens is still honest); hooks (harness, not store semantics). Two structural findings: (a) aggregation vertices own NO store today, so their constitution history (combine membership over time) has no home — implies every vertex, even aggregations, needs at least an internal table; rewinding an aggregate without membership history is dishonest the same way rewinding under today's ontology is. (b) The regress terminates one level up: internal-table rows are kind-ed by a FIXED code-defined meta-schema (vertex-state, membership-change, grant-change, tick), not by the vertex itself — the store describes its own attention topology over time, but the language it describes it IN is frozen, so no infinite regress.

high      21:22 [thread] vertex-state-in-store: The .vertex is the last mutable, provenance-free thing in an immutable system — and Rewind makes that a correctness problem: --asof replays facts through TODAY'S ontology, an anachronistic graph, because vertex evolution is unrecorded. Kyle's converging design (2026-07-01): stores grow a table for INTERNAL data generally (ticks already are one — system self-description vs domain observations), one occupant being vertex state over time. The file becomes a working copy/checkout; the store holds canonical history; the existing vertex-mutating commands become provenanced writes; prior materialize-in/out work (.loop forms) becomes the checkout mechanism. Consequences to design: rewind gains two time axes (facts-asof, ontology-asof; default equal for honesty, --ontology=now for deliberate reinterpretation); vertex-state rows should enter the tick/signing chain so ontology history is ATTESTABLE (agent-attestation convergence: what facts meant at T is itself signed); general principle candidate: anything that changes how facts are READ must itself be historized, or rewind lies.

high      18:25 [decision] architecture/typed-edges-late-bound-promotion: Kyle's requirement reframes the typed-edge design: capture must be declaration-free and in-the-moment (emit stakeholder=X naturally during a session); declaration comes LATER as a vertex edit that 'shows' the edge. Graph EDGE-membership (salience, --refs, predicate label) is declaration-gated. (3) This MOVES the build seam. Prior turn I said materialize at the resolve/emit path; late-binding kills that (it would freeze the ontology at capture). Seam moves to FOLD CONSTRUCTION: thread the edge declaration lang->atoms into _make_upsert/_make_collect so collection reflects the CURRENT vertex over all history. (4) Footgun dissolves without gating capture -- accidental captures (topic_ref) stay inert unless someone declares them an edge. tail      18:36 [observation] rendering/painted-table-fit-needs-fill: painted gotcha caught by adversarial review: table(overflow=Overflow.FIT) only SHRINKS Fill columns. A table built entirely from fixed-int or AUTO columns IGNORES the width budget — it renders at natural width and overflows narrow terminals, while a card capped to width disagrees. The fix that honours width: declare the one variable column as Fill() with min_width + max_width=natural — fills to natural on a roomy terminal, shrinks+ellipsizes when the budget is tight (FIT can act). Below the irreducible floor (fixed numeric cols + gaps), drop a decorative column (we drop TREND under width 64). Also: table() reverse-videos row 0 by default (TUI cursor) — pass selected_style=Style() for a static listing; and use Wrap.ELLIPSIS not the default hard-clip on card sublines so narrow widths signal loss with a marker. Reusable for any painted table consumer.

My earlier claim (bare-name->aggregation) read only the generic resolver, which is step 3 of dispatch. NET for plugin: agent-facing text keeps bare 'sl emit project ...'; the HOOK uses explicit ${CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR}/.loops/project.vertex — NOT because bare-name is broken but because a hook must not RELY on cwd==project-root (emit dispatch IS cwd-aware; the hook's cwd is not contract-guaranteed, CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR is). Plus: all hook entry points must guard on [ -f $V ] so a user-scope plugin no-ops cleanly in non-loops repos.

tail      18:31 [decision] design/cli-grammar-uniform-verb-first: DECIDED (Kyle 2026-06-29): remove vertex-first dispatch ENTIRELY — option (b) full uniformity over (a) keep-bare-read. Every invocation becomes verb-first `sl <verb> <vertex> ...`; arg0 is ALWAYS a verb/command, ZERO ambiguity. Consequences: (1) bare implicit-read goes — `sl project` -> `sl read project` everywhere; (2) verbs take the vertex UNIFORMLY as first positional — cite gains a vertex arg `sl cite <vertex> REF...` consistent with emit (the grammar-level fix for the cite asymmetry, not a doc patch); (3) population ops migrate to top-level `sl add <vertex> ...` (COMMANDS already supports it) — `sl reading add foo url` -> `sl add reading foo url`. DELETES the bulk of cli/app.py intricacy: _vertex_first, _identify_op_token (op-past-global-flags scan), _is_predicate_token, the _peel_observer before/after-op split, VERTEX_OPS, the population-op argv reconstruction, the tier-3 router. RATIONALE: correctness (one grammar per verb; a vertex named like a verb cannot shadow it) + simplification (most of the dispatcher dissolves) + it kills friction:vertex-first-dispatch-legacy-complexity and dissolves friction:loops-skill-cite-syntax-wrong at the root. MIGRATION (part of the build): audit + update hooks (grep clean so far), docs (CLAUDE.md, CLI-CHEATSHEET), the global loops skill examples, and muscle-memory; the bare-vertex form disappears from all of them. Build is its own focused session (touches the live dispatch every agent + hook rides). Sequence: likely after the plugin packaging, since the plugin consolidates the hooks/skill that this migration also touches.
mid       18:14 [friction] vertex-first-dispatch-legacy-complexity: Vertex-first dispatch (tier 3: sl <vertex> <verb>) is convenience-era complexity from when the CLI was small (Kyle 2026-06-29) — removing it is a CORRECTNESS + SIMPLIFICATION win and dissolves the cite-syntax asymmetry at its ROOT (friction:loops-skill-cite-syntax-wrong was the symptom). It bundles TWO jobs: (1) bare implicit-read `sl project`->read (high-value shorthand); (2) vertex-first OP `sl project cite`/`sl reading add` (legacy duplication of verb-first). Job 2 is the friction: emit takes the vertex AFTER the verb (sl emit <vertex>) but cite has no vertex slot, so vertex-first was the ONLY way to target a vertex with cite -> two grammars, one asymmetry, easy to mis-document. REMOVING tier-3 deletes the bulk of app.py intricacy: _vertex_first, _identify_op_token (op-past-global-flags), _is_predicate_token, the _peel_observer before/after-op split, VERTEX_OPS + population-op argv reconstruction. CORRECTNESS: one grammar per verb; eliminates the "is arg0 a vertex or unknown command?" class (a vertex named like a verb cannot shadow it). REQUIRED COMPANION: verbs take the vertex UNIFORMLY as a positional — cite gains a vertex arg (sl cite <vertex> REF), consistent with emit — a grammar that cannot be mis-stated, the structural fix vs a doc patch. OPEN DECISION (shapes the work): fate of bare implicit-read sl project->read — (a) keep it as a narrow rule + reserve verb names (verb wins on collision), removing only the op form; or (b) full uniformity sl <verb> <vertex> everywhere, zero arg0 ambiguity but sl project->sl read project. Automation already uses verb-first (low migration risk, grep of hooks/config clean); the human-facing change is the implicit-read shorthand. Design+build deserves its own focused session (touches the live dispatch every agent + hook uses).
mid       17:51 [friction] loops-skill-cite-syntax-wrong: The now-global loops skill documented cite as `sl cite <vertex> kind:key ...` — WRONG, and it bit me on the first real cite this session: cite has NO vertex positional (it is dissolved into emit; all positionals are refs), so `project` became a stray ref and the cite landed in the cwd-inferred vertex (not project) with every decision ref dropped. CORRECT forms: vertex-first `sl <vertex> cite REF REF -m` (targets a named vertex, sets ctx.vertex_path) OR cwd-local `sl cite REF REF -m` (from a vertex dir). ROOT of the trap: emit takes the vertex as a positional (`sl emit <vertex> KIND`), cite does NOT — an asymmetry easy to mis-document. FIXED the skill cite line in the same change. Validates friction:loops-skill-canonical-source-gitignored live: the skill is now canonical infra, so an error in it propagates to every repo agent — caught here only because I exercised it.

tail      16:38 [observation] architecture/cross-store-ref-resolution: VERIFIED model (2026-06-29, traced + reproduced) — corrects my earlier overstatement that "cross-store refs do not resolve." They do; the navigable address ALWAYS survives. Three layers: (1) EMIT-TIME PIN — _resolve_one walks the root-cwd topology (combine/discover chain) and pins the target current ULID into a {field}_ref sibling; resolves ONLY if the target store is in the emit cwd topology. Out-of-topology emit prints WARN "ref did not resolve — dropped", but that drops only the PIN, not the ref. (2) NAVIGABLE ADDRESS — the kind:key value is preserved verbatim in item.refs regardless of pin success (confirmed: painted seed fact retains [decision:design/completion-dissolves-into-painted, ...] in refs after a "dropped" WARN). (3) READ-SIDE GRAPH — _compute_inbound_edges is ADDRESS-keyed (kind/key, colon/slash normalized) and store-local to the READ. CONSEQUENCE: a cross-repo ref resolves in the GRAPH when read through a topology that combines both ends — reproduced: loops target inbound=1 via the cli-completion aggregation (combines loops+painted), inbound=0 read loops-alone (harmless dangling). So cross-store ref resolution is a TOPOLOGY-MEMBERSHIP property (a combine-block config choice), not a hard limit — this is the basis for the on-demand arc-aggregation pattern. CAVEAT: the emit-time pin is a ULID snapshot, fragile across independent store rebirth; the address is durable and the graph runs on it, so a dangling pin is cosmetic-provenance, not a lost edge.

tail      16:10 [observation] pattern/dispatch-help-completion-three-reflections: One argparse parser, three reflections: PARSE (run the command), HELP (render arg defs), COMPLETE (emit candidates). Generalizes: when a framework reflects a structure for N purposes, the N+1th reflection of the SAME structure belongs at the same layer, not a layer up. Instance of "anything painted can do, prefer painted" (decision/design/full-painted-integration-residue). Connects to read-path-features-over-noticing-skills at the tooling layer: completion is a read-path feature of the parser, not a separately-maintained artifact.

mid       02:19 [friction] read-tty-truncation-not-defeatable: Audit-confirmed and widened into a family: on a TTY the human has NO in-band way to get full fidelity. (a) --plain flips reporter.use_ansi but never reporter.width, so it cannot un-truncate the TTY layout. (b) --match event-row bodies are hard-capped at 80 chars regardless of terminal width, --full, or zoom -- no escape. (c) fact-body (--facts) truncation is len/codepoint-based (loops-local elide, _helpers.py:20-36) not wcwidth, so CJK over-clips and the ellipsis itself gets eaten by the outer Wrap.NONE. (d) -v truncates the body HARDER than SUMMARY and drops the [+Nc] marker (silent). --full/-v/-vv are all inert on these axes; only piping to cat recovers. Root: the search/fact-body paths bypass the painted width/wcwidth allocator the fold path honors (cli-render-rebuild residue). Fix: forward lens width (None=no-cap) into content_gist plus elide, honor r.granularity for --full, route through budget_fields/truncate_ellipsis, and add a width override seam (--plain or a new --wide sets reporter.width=None) so a TTY user gets the untruncated layout in-band.
mid       02:19 [friction] secondary-lines-clip-without-marker: Dangerous silent clip. On a TTY the body/label line announces width truncation (ellipsis plus [+Nc]) but the secondary lines (refs, observer, id, metadata) clip with NO marker -- bare Block.text Wrap.NONE. A clipped ref reads as a real, different fold key, so the human can mis-read which fact is referenced. Within a single record, two different truncation disciplines. Fix: route secondary lines through the same marker discipline (Wrap.ELLIPSIS / block_truncate) so every width-clipped line appends an ellipsis consistently.
mid       02:19 [friction] facts-empty-for-collect-fold-kinds: Contract inversion. --facts is documented show raw fact stream but renders EMPTY for collect-fold kinds (cite/change/log/seal): sl read project --facts --kind cite shows zero rows under a No history footer despite 36 real cite facts. mid       02:19 [friction] live-mode-hangs-silently-on-pipe: Hard bug. sl read project --live to a pipe produces 0 bytes and never exits (must SIGKILL); on a TTY it renders a live alt-screen. _resolve_mode (fold.py:292) returns live on args.live with NO is_tty guard; painted runner.py:338-356 non-ansi _run_live calls print_block only AFTER an unbounded async-for over an infinite generator, so for any infinite stream on a pipe the loop never ends and zero bytes are emitted. 1.21MB of Surface content is reachable by every non-live path. mid       02:19 [friction] fold-lens-render-diverges-from-faithful-surface: THE central divergence. The plain/styled fold lens REORDERS (head item salience 15 vs --json rows[0] salience 1, disjoint) and DROPS rows (297 of 502 decisions windowed out by the salience-greater-than-1 group cut) as its BASE order, while --json/to_dict emits surface.rows verbatim. This contradicts surface.py:20-23 own stated invariant (same rows, same order) and to_dict:734 falsely claims same ranked rows the lens renders. Worse: window.shown==total==502, limited_by==null -- the provenance silently tells consumers the render is COMPLETE while 297 rows are hidden. Human and agent see different row SETS in different ORDERS, unannounced and not in-band defeatable. Fix: drop the lens base pre-sort (fold.py:463/476/550), make ranking plus windowing opt-in via Surface.budget so Window records shown-less-than-total plus limited_by=salience-window; add in-band --all to expand. mid       02:19 [observation] design/curation-belongs-in-surface-not-renderers: Audit verdict (w6d4zptvv, 37 agents): Surface IS the renderer-invariant fixed point -- an invariance probe proved context (is_tty/zoom/width/mode/format) does NOT leak into Surface construction; --json was byte-identical (md5 0601dcfd) across pipe, COLUMNS 80 and 400, and -q/-v/-vv. So the umwelt-fork is NOT a no-common-reality problem; it is that the renderers RE-CURATE the shared Surface behind its back. The fold lens applies salience reorder plus namespace windowing as its BASE projection while to_dict emits surface.rows verbatim -- two different curations of one Surface, neither announcing which it holds. Reframe / dissolution: promote curation OUT of the renderers and INTO Surface as a declared, serialized budget (Window provenance), computed once and emitted in --json. Then every renderer collapses to render(Surface, context) with zero independent loss, the umwelt-difference between any two views becomes a computable Window-diff, and the aggressive curation a human-orient redesign needs is done ONCE with provenance and is one in-band keystroke from reversal. The constraint is not add-instrumentation; it is stop-the-renderers-from-curating, let-Surface-own-it. Grow-the-substrate over fork-the-consumer.

mid       01:42 [observation] design/umwelt-fork-no-shared-reality: The same read renders a materially different reality depending on output context. Human-on-TTY sees width-clipped truncated styled output; agent-on-pipe sees the full plain render. mid       01:42 [friction] read-tty-truncation-not-defeatable: On a TTY there is no in-band way to view a full body. --full (force full-body granularity) does not defeat the terminal-width clip: a complete-key address still renders [+920c] truncated. -v truncates the body even harder AND drops the [+920c] elision marker, so the loss becomes silent. Only piping to cat (dropping to the non-TTY plain renderer) shows the whole body. Width-clip is correct orient behavior leaking into the read path; addressing one complete key is a read, not an orient.
mid       01:42 [friction] read-address-separator-colon-vs-slash: Positional read address uses slash (kind/key) but every ref uses colon (kind:key). tail      19:47 [observation] design/orient-salience-is-distinct-from-read-salience: Salience-FF map surfaced the crux answer in EVIDENCE: orient ranking != read ranking, and Surface only materializes the read one. All 3 session-open lenses (session_start, session_landing, identity_prompt) are ORIENT surfaces; the in-repo fold lens is the READ drill-in and windows PURELY by salience (n+inbound). Neither has a Surface analogue. So Surface.salience = n+inbound = IMPORTANCE, timeless = a READ salience; ORIENT needs importance + recency + change-state. Implication for thread:human-umwelt-static-view: the human static view is NOT read-styled-with-salience; orient is a richer ranking the Surface should materialize as first-class (recency + change-marks), instead of each orient lens bolting it on by hand divergently. mid       15:49 [friction] emit-ref-resolution-colon-blind: ROOT CAUSE (pre-existing, surfaced on S8 smoke tour): emit-time entity-ref resolution only handles SLASH-form refs (kind/key). But the CANONICAL documented form is COLON (ref=decision:design/foo, ref=thread:arc-name — every CLAUDE.md/skill/identity example). Live census .loops/data/project.db (2622 facts): colon refs 499 total / 0 resolved; slash refs 220 / 32 resolved. So write-time typo/stale-ref WARN, ref_ref ULID materialization, AND S6's new -v inbound-delta are ALL dead for colon refs. tail      05:58 [decision] implementation/search-scopes-fts-to-present-kinds: S5 self-review catch: vertex_search returns facts across ALL indexed kinds, ignoring a --kind filter (which only narrowed the post-fetch surface, not vertex_search's view). So --kind decision --match foo would leak FTS hits from other indexed kinds. Fix: scope the FTS path to fts_kinds = present & indexed (present already reflects the fetch-time --kind narrowing), and unindexed = present - indexed. FTS covers present&indexed, substring covers present-but-not-indexed; the two are disjoint by construction so no fact double-counts. Test: test_search_fts_respects_kind_scoped_surface.

tail      05:47 [decision] design/count-before-budget-ordering: S4 transform order is filter->select->count->budget (count BEFORE budget). count() emits one row per group in count-desc order with salience=count; a following budget(limit=N) then takes the top-N GROUPS by count (the sort|uniq -c|sort|head semantic). mid       00:44 [decision] design/declare-observer-print-not-write: Resolved (Kyle, 2026-06-27): --declare-observer is PRINT-NOT-WRITE. loops does NOT mutate the .vertex — it PRINTS the exact observers{} entry + its location, and the actor (agents Edit tool / human) applies it. Rationale: (1) the forgive path (WARN+store, Row carries observer regardless) already kills the 15 #1 errors with ZERO write-back, so --declare-observer is pure convenience-persist; (2) observers{} is also the KEY REGISTRY that verifies tick signatures (design/observer-key-registry) — auto-writing it would mint trust material into loops own attestation substrate; (3) the consumer is an agent with file-edit tools, so the actor can apply a printed entry. The real fork was write-vs-print, UPSTREAM of the docs append-vs-round-trip rec — which is NOT taken. Print dissolves the KDL-writer, the concurrent-writer race, and the round-trip-fidelity question entirely. Resolves thread:declare-observer-write-back; supersedes the docs minimal-append rec for open-decision #3.
mid       00:12 [thread] declare-observer-write-back: OPEN (Kyle wants to discuss, 2026-06-27). #3 of the surface open-decisions. Reframed OFF the docs append-vs-round-trip axis onto two upstream questions. (A) TRUST-REGISTRY ENTANGLEMENT — observers{} is also the key registry (ObserverDecl.key; design/observer-key-registry: the registry IS the vertex file, used to verify tick signatures). So --declare-observer either writes a NAME-ONLY entry (half a registration: observer can emit but is unverifiable in a signing vertex) or NAME+KEY (programmatically minting trust material). The forgive-path already kills the 15 errors with NO write-back; --declare-observer is pure convenience-persist, and what it persists sets its risk class. (B) ACTOR-MODEL DISSOLUTION — the consumer is an agent with file-edit tools, so --declare-observer could just PRINT the exact observers{} entry + location and let the actor (agent Edit / human) apply it, dissolving the KDL-writer entirely and keeping loops out of silently mutating its own trust registry. Lean: write-vs-print is upstream of append-vs-round-trip; if print, the fidelity question evaporates.

mid       23:55 [decision] design/views-fundamental-lens-is-a-render: Vocabulary firmed (Kyle, 2026-06-27): the VIEW is the fundamental authoring unit — a named selection over the Surface, declared as data in a vertex views{} block; a LENS is demoted to "a render" — the optional Surface->Block encoder kernel a view references. view ⊋ lens: a Tier-A pure-selection view has no lens at all. Consequence for the vertex file: it declares TWO blocks not three — loops{} (the kinds+fold/search/preview vocabulary) + views{} (named selections over it). A lens is NEVER declared in the vertex, only referenced by name (render "X") and resolved as a Python module on the existing 4-tier path. lens{} dissolves into views{} (it was always the degenerate whole-surface view + custom render); kept as deprecated sugar compiling to a ViewDecl for one release, then LensDecl/_load_lens_block/VertexFile.lens are swept. Residue cleared same change: the stream pointer dies (stream verb dissolves, FTS re-binds onto read --match); the fold overload clears (loops.<kind>.fold stays fold-strategy by/collect, the render module is named by render not a second fold). mid       17:45 [decision] design/granularity-by-complete-key-address: Granularity crux resolved (Kyles call, 2026-06-27): read returns a facts WHOLE body when addressed by a COMPLETE fold-key (read decision --key design/foo) -- unique within kind by the fold-upsert contract, so deterministic, NOT cardinality-dependent. A prefix (--key design/) or content-filter (--match) returns headlines. --full forces bodies for any N rows. Chosen over explicit-only (loses the one-shot win on a named fact) and auto-on-singular (the integrations original rule -- shape depends on result-set size, breaks addressed-read=body trust when a 2nd fact lands). Resolves stress risk #1 (granularity-by-cardinality). The other pre-build risk (FTS confirm asymmetry) resolves by steering confirm-after-emit to --last + a loud not-indexed coverage signal. Slice 1 (the Surface keystone) bakes this in.
mid       17:33 [observation] design/two-pre-build-risks-surface: Stress-test surfaced two risks to resolve BEFORE building the Surface keystone (2026-06-27): (1) GRANULARITY-BY-CARDINALITY -- the integration auto-returns the whole body when a filtered read collapses to one row, making output SHAPE depend on result-set size (a read that returns a body today returns headlines tomorrow when a second fact lands). Breaks the load-bearing addressed-read=body trust -> agents reroute to sqlite again. Fix: make whole an explicit address property, not a runtime row-count side effect. (2) FTS CONFIRM ASYMMETRY -- the read/write symmetry (emit re-enters the read seam) is FALSE on the search axis: a just-emitted fact is unsearchable via --match until re-index, so emit->read --match->nothing-landed->panic->sqlite manufactures the exact reroute were eliminating. Fix: steer confirm-after-emit to --last (entity/ts axis), make the coverage signal loud.
high      17:33 [decision] design/surface-architecture-pared-to-keystone: Stress-tested architecture (2026-06-27). Core: a frozen Surface value (flat ordered Rows + per-kind KindView render-hints + a Window provenance record) interposed at the dispatch seam between fetch and render. A Row = a FoldItem plus materialized inbound/salience + an address; built ~1:1 from atoms. All ops (search/filter/select/budget/count/whole) are typed transforms on the Surface BEFORE either encoder runs; render(plain/styled) and to_dict(json) are the last optional step -> json/plain parity. Net-new is SMALL (one painted-free surface.py + the four salience helpers LIFTED from fold.py byte-for-byte); most pains close via dissolution/re-bind. The keystone survives the dissolution test for ONE precise reason: json/plain parity + server-side projection need a structured intermediate that is neither FoldState nor Block; a few flags cannot serve that. STRESS PARED BACK (build ahead of measured need): SHIP keystone + render-only encoders + eq-only predicate + emit grammar fixes + retract; DEFER views{}-as-data authoring framework, neq/prefix operators, Tier-C transform modules, gc/migrate, interactive TUI -- all behind observed demand. Full design: docs/dev/structured-surface-architecture-2026-06-27.md.
mid       17:04 [decision] design/structured-fact-surface-spine: Redesign spine (Kyles call, 2026-06-27): one fetch -> a structured, addressable fact surface -> renderers; agent-first, plain default on non-TTY. search/fact-whole/budget/projection operate on the SURFACE not on rendered text; lenses = named views over the surface; styled + interactive human renderers are a LATER tier on the same surface (human umwelt unmeasured -> design the seam, instrument before committing). Chosen over tactical-fixes-only because the 5 measured agent needs (plain, search, fact-whole, budget, projection) are instances of ONE root cause: the lens renders a monolithic ANSI block too early, before the data is addressable. Patterns-over-point-solutions: interpose the addressable surface, make styled rendering the last optional step. Next: architecture-design workflow.
mid       16:10 [decision] design/content-search-rebind-not-build: Verified dissolution finding (2026-06-27): the #1 usage gap (no content-search; 65pct of 456 greps hunt fact NAMES, 155 payload-LIKE + 152 json_extract reroutes, worst burst 27 consecutive LIKE) is NOT missing capability. engine.vertex_search (FTS5 over payloads, vertex_reader.py:1319) + StoreReader.search_facts (store_reader.py:290) already exist AND are already wired to the CLI via commands/fetch.py:326 — but stranded on the near-dead stream verb as a positional fallback, not a discoverable read flag. Fix = RE-BIND search onto read (read --grep/--match over names+bodies + multi-name), not build new plumbing. Highest-leverage single move and a pure dissolution. Caught by the completeness critic, verified against source.
mid       16:10 [decision] practice/usage-inverts-the-renderer-thesis: Usage forensics (siftd, 8.5K loops calls, 2026-06-27) inverts the redesign thesis. The dominant consumer of read is an AGENT that wants plain/searchable/sliceable/fact-whole text and REJECTS the styled render: --plain is the single hottest flag in the whole CLI (25.2pct of all calls, 58.1pct of reads), --json near-cold (2.9pct); 67.9-70.2pct of reads are piped through head/grep/tail; 21.8pct of store reads bypass the CLI to raw sqlite. So leverage-the-renderer aimed at the wrong consumer: the styled render is a HUMAN-tier concern, and the human umwelt has ZERO rows in the corpus (unfalsifiable). Static-first = AGENT-CONTRACT-first. Two umwelts: agent (plain+search+fact-whole+budget+projection, measured, dominant) vs human (styled+interactive, unmeasured, judgment+instrument). The interactive tree-drill design is a human-tier second layer we would currently be designing blind. Full report: docs/dev/loops-usage-forensics-2026-06-27.md.
mid       15:47 [observation] practice/usage-grounding-before-ui-redesign: Raw siftd signal before forensic synthesis (2026-06-27): 8569 sl/loops invocations + 761 sqlite3-against-loops reroutes globally across 406 workspaces. Sample read commands show the static read path is consumed almost entirely through shell post-filters: sl read --kind X --key Y | head -100, | grep -i trace, --facts | head -200, --plain | grep -E. Two gaps visible pre-analysis: (1) missing content-search (agents pipe to grep for substring), (2) verbosity (agents pipe to head to truncate). The reroute IS the say/do seam made measurable: system says read is the interface; 761 sqlite escapes + pervasive grep/head say otherwise.

mid       19:03 [decision] design/devtools-help-args-idiom: SUPERSEDES design/devtools-run-cli-args-bridge. The devtools (test/compile/validate) hand-rolled -h dissolves via painted 0.3.0's pre-parse + describe-for-help idiom: pre-parse the command's own args (argparse add_help=False), pass help_args=[HelpArg(name, desc, positional=)] to run_cli so --help lists them, fetch closes over the pre-parsed namespace. NOT the build_fidelity capture (that was the 0.2.0 bridge) and NOT the Operation/dispatch IR (devtools carry pass/fail exit codes dispatch STATIC drops). -h-vs-required-positional wrinkle: validate (nargs=*) lets -h reach run_cli freely; compile/test guard a required file, so a bare help request routes to run_cli's help renderer BEFORE the guard (help short-circuits pre-fetch). This is the proven pattern store inherits.
mid       19:03 [thread] painted-run-cli-args-seam: RESOLVED by painted 0.3.0 (committed 8518b3c loops-side). Painted answered the seam NOT with my proposed CliContext.args / fetch(ctx), but with a different blessed idiom: HelpArg + run_cli(help_args=[...]) — 'for commands that pre-parse their own args before calling run_cli, describe them so they appear in --help'. So the command keeps its inherent pre-parse (needed for values + branching anyway), fetch closes over the parsed namespace directly, and help_args makes painted's --help list them. Cleaner than exposing the namespace through CliContext — the parse stays the command's, painted only renders the description. devtools build_fidelity capture bridge collapsed onto this. Same idiom is the store conversion path. Lesson: proposed a seam shape, painted shipped a better-fitting one; the gap was real, the fix wasn't my shape.
high      18:30 [decision] design/budget-fields-truncation-gate-contract: painted shipped budget_fields (74b4103, stable tier, wcwidth-measured, BudgetFit(text,dropped)). It carved a principled contract that DIVERGES from loops' field-tested _render_preview: min_field gates TRUNCATION ONLY (render longest contiguous prefix where each field fits whole OR truncates to >= min_field), so short WHOLE values loops currently drops are kept. loops' guard was over-broad — dropped any field whose slot < min_field even when the whole value fit, conflating 'slot small' with 'drop'. DECISION: adopt painted's contract FRESH (no bug-for-bug parity revert). Rationale: min_field's honest purpose is anti-nub (prevent truncated fragments), not anti-presence; dropping whole short values is the actual second bug (wcwidth/CJK len() was the first). Strictly more informative, same prefix shape, width-exactness law holds, nothing keys off field-absence (preview is informational, not load-bearing).
