mid       17:58 [thread] painted-run-cli-args-seam: GAP found during rebuild step 4 (devtools shim conversion): painted run_cli can own --help for a command's own args via the add_args(parser) hook, but CliContext (passed to fetch/render) exposes only fidelity/mode/use_ansi/is_tty/width/height — NOT the parsed namespace. So a run_cli command that needs its own positionals/options in fetch (devtools: files/--input/--limit; store: db path + subcommands) has no clean way to read them back. Today the ONLY hook seeing the namespace is build_fidelity(namespace, fidelity). PROPOSAL to painted: expose parsed args to the command — either CliContext.args (the Namespace) or allow fetch(ctx)->T. Same bar as A2: real consumer (every run_cli command needing its own args) + general nameable seam. BRIDGE adopted meanwhile (Kyle's call): single add_args declaration + capture namespace via build_fidelity into a closure, ref this thread, temporary until the seam lands.

mid       15:52 [friction] shell-oneliner-punctuation-and-wordsplit: Repeat pattern (3+ instances): one-liner Bash calls mangled by (a) non-ascii punctuation sneaking in — full-width semicolon U+FF1B, zsh-significant '=' — and (b) zsh word-splitting of unquoted lists + non-persistent cwd across compound commands. Mitigation that reliably fires: prefer 'grep -rl ... | while IFS= read -r f' over for-loops on unquoted $(...), keep cwd-setting in the same compound line, and avoid semicolon-dense one-liners (use heredoc scripts for multi-step). mid       23:50 [decision] design/disclosure-vs-domain-query-axis: COHERENCE FINDING reframing rebuild step 3. The design doc (rebuild-design-0.4.0.md §1) assumed loops' --facts/--refs/--diff dissolve into painted Tags gated by ctx.fidelity.shows(). Grounding in fold.py disproves it: all three are DOMAIN-QUERY SELECTORS, not disclosure layers. --diff selects a different fetcher (_build_diff_fetch + trace lens); --facts toggles want_facts (folded vs raw stream); --refs N carries a traversal DEPTH into fetch (painted's store_true Tag can't model the N). painted's Tag model assumes fixed data revealed in named layers; loops' flags change the query itself. So the real dissolution boundary: PURE TERMINAL axes (-q/-v depth, --max-chars/-lines budgets, --plain/--json format, --static/--live/-i mode) dissolve into painted add_cli_args+parse_fidelity; DOMAIN-QUERY selectors (--facts/--diff/--refs) stay loops-side (they parameterize fetch). This follows directly from grow-painted-over-workaround + 'push loops into domain-specific arenas' (Kyle): query selection IS domain, not terminal. Step 3 revised: dissolve the generic terminal flags per view; keep domain flags; merge their loops-computed visibility into the painted-compiled Fidelity.

high      22:09 [decision] design/full-painted-integration-residue: What 'build the CLI fully on painted' reduces to (confirmed against painted 0.2.0 source). mid       22:09 [decision] design/cli-context-phase-split: Keystone resolution: the two CliContext classes dissolve by PHASE, not merge. painted's CliContext (fidelity,mode,use_ansi,is_tty,width,height) = RENDER-phase state; loops' (reporter,vertex_path,vertex_name,observer,loops_home,isatty) = FETCH/DISPATCH-phase state. They are different kinds of thing in different phases of one command — never co-occur in a single call. So we do NOT extend painted's frozen dataclass (fights the framework). Instead: rename loops' CliContext -> Invocation (domain phase: vertex resolution, signer injection, observer-as-selector, store handle); the render phase receives painted's ctx unchanged; lenses become (ctx: painted.CliContext, data) -> Block and never see vertex paths/signers. fetch() is the bridge: Invocation opens store + folds + returns data, painted calls the lens with its own ctx. This removes the mixed-feed the audit flagged (legacy commands/ get painted ctx, views/ get loops'). Keystone step blocks all of 4a.
mid       21:59 [decision] design/cli-context-keystone-shape: Gate made the CliContext keystone concrete. The two classes are NOT near-duplicates to merge — they carry ORTHOGONAL concerns sharing a name. painted-0.2.0 CliContext = (fidelity, mode, use_ansi, is_tty, width, height): terminal/rendering state (note zoom->fidelity rename is the exact drift that broke tasks). loops CliContext (loops/cli/context.py) = (reporter, vertex_path, vertex_name, observer): dispatch/domain state. The rebuild's 'loops CliContext becomes a thin extension of painted.cli.CliContext' is therefore COMPOSITION not unification: loops' domain fields wrap/hold a painted render-context, they don't flatten into one constructor. Confirms keystone-first sequencing: reconcile by composition before touching dispatch. tasks' x7 failures are the canary — they'll be fixed by the same reconciliation (s/zoom=/fidelity=/ at minimum, or routing through the composed context).

tail      18:50 [thread] rebirth-keyless-attestation-drop: OPEN posture question surfaced by review #2 (and named in rebirth.py's floor-exemption comment). "loops store rebirth" with no tick_signer mints an UNSIGNED genesis tick — silently dropping a signed source lineage's attestation. This is NOT a floor bypass: rebirth starts a fresh chain (pre-era, verify ok=True), and the CLI does print "genesis tick unsigned". But it is asymmetric with reanchor, which REFUSES without a key ("a signed fact must not lose authorship"). QUESTION: should keyless rebirth of a SIGNED source likewise refuse (or require an explicit --allow-unsigned), or is silently starting a fresh unsigned lineage the correct posture for a migration/rebirth? Turns on whether rebirth means "continue this lineage" (-> refuse, like reanchor) or "fork a new custody context" (-> unsigned start is fine). Connects to the tick-signing floor (fresh-lineage exemption) and the reanchor refusal precedent.

mid       18:50 [observation] practice/adversarial-review-catches-what-confidence-misses: Two-round adversarial review (Workflow, 15 agents each) of the seal-era-guard arc caught TWO real holes that solo confidence missed — after I had said "pretty confident we're good." Round 1 (on 9f2de91, verb-scoped guard): HIGH — the guard sat on the seal VERB, but "sl emit <v> seal" fires the same boundary via cmd_emit, a one-token bypass of the floor. A store-level invariant cannot be enforced at the verb. Round 2 (on 6c368e4, after moving the guard to the engine mint): MEDIUM — Vertex._store_tick is NOT the only live mint (apps/tasks' harness emit_tick is a second), so enforce_floor=False was fail-OPEN; a forgotten caller silently bypassed the invariant. Both fixes were dissolutions the reviews named: (1) move enforcement from the verb to the store mint; (2) flip the default to fail-SAFE (enforce by default, name the exemptions). PATTERN for a security/integrity invariant: (a) enforce at the single lowest chokepoint, not at each call site; (b) make enforcement the DEFAULT with named opt-outs, never opt-in — both "where" and "default polarity" are load-bearing, and adversarial review surfaced them precisely because the holes were the cases my framing assumed away ("single mint point", "covers the hook"). One refinement of the review itself: checking append_tick's callers BEFORE applying the reviewer's literal "guard in append_tick" caught that it is shared with rebirth/slice — the right seam was narrower than the review's first suggestion. Review informs; caller-analysis decides placement.

high      17:42 [thread] seal-era-boundary-guard: IMPLEMENTED (scoped to the seal verb) 2026-06-14, commit 9f2de91. Both halves of decision:design/tick-signing-era-is-a-floor landed: (1) DISCLOSURE — the boundary receipt now prints "· signed" / "· unsigned" (emit.py), so a minted tick's signing outcome is never silent. (2) GUARD — seal.py refuses (clean error, exit 1, no fact emitted, no tick minted) when the store is in the signed era (has signed ticks) AND no key is available; a pre-era (never-signed) store sealing unsigned proceeds; --dry-run is exempt; also narrowed a latent writable=None path the old code dereferenced unguarded. Verified empirically across all three truth-table branches: keyed+signed-era → signs + "· signed" (exit 0); no-key+signed-era → REFUSE, chain stays intact, no unsigned tick minted (exit 1); no-key+pre-era → mints unsigned + "· unsigned" (exit 0). 4 new tests (the three branches + dry-run exemption); 1326 app tests pass, no regressions. This covers BOTH sl seal and the SessionEnd hook (the real-world silent-corruption path) because the hook seals through the same verb. REMAINING — thread stays open: (a) promote the guard into the ENGINE mint so emit-triggered (count-based) boundaries are also covered — carries the implicit-vs-explicit-trigger wrinkle (refuse the whole emit vs defer just the boundary), Kyle's call; (b) Gate A, the forward "require signing" vertex flag, remains separate and unspecified. tail      17:24 [thread] transport-era-signing-key-flow: Forward problem flagged by Kyle 2026-06-14 while ratifying the tick-signing floor (decision:design/tick-signing-era-is-a-floor): the SSH "key is always local" assumption that makes signing low-friction breaks in the transport era. Refinement that surfaced: what gets "passed around" is PUBLIC keys (verification), never PRIVATE keys (signing) — SSH all the way down, the private half never leaves the machine. Public-key distribution is largely already designed in the vouch / agent-attestation substrate (JWKS topology, IssuerRegistry dispatch by iss, issuer->namespace mapping) and in the .vertex observers{} registry. The genuinely-NEW problem is CHAIN RECONCILIATION ON MERGE: when store B ingests signed facts from store A (sqlmerge), B's tick chain must absorb A's signed facts WITHOUT (a) re-signing them — that erases A's authorship — or (b) minting an unsigned merge-boundary tick — the Gate-B floor forbids that. So: who mints and signs the boundary tick over a merged window, with what authority, and how does B's era-monotonicity hold across a merge of two independently-signed chains? This is where the tick-signing floor gets its teeth in the multi-store world. Connects to sqlmerge (libs/store transport), Peer/Grant, and the deferred verify-on-receive consumer that reactivates fact-signing enforcement.
high      17:24 [decision] design/tick-signing-era-is-a-floor: Kyle ratified 2026-06-14 (Gate-B floor): once a store starts signing at the TICK level, it must continue — the era-regression guard (no unsigned tick after a signed tick) is a non-negotiable FLOOR, not a per-vertex flag. Rationale: era-monotonicity is witness-chain INTEGRITY, not vertex POLICY — verify already condemns the regressed state (CHAIN BROKEN) and reanchor already refuses to create it; seal must match (closes the say/do gap where seal could mint exactly what verify forbids). Friction is low in the SSH sense: the private key is local, so signing is transparent/automatic while present; the cost only appears when the key is ABSENT, and then the right behavior is SSH's — a hard STOP, never a silent downgrade to unauthenticated. So seal REFUSES (not warn-and-proceed) to mint an unsigned tick in the signed era. Degrades gracefully: emit stays opportunistic so the window's FACTS are still stored; only the attestation boundary (tick) is withheld, and the next successful seal closes the accumulated window — data preserved, attestation deferred, never falsified. Disclosure is the floor under all of it: every signing action states signed/unsigned + reason regardless of the refuse/proceed branch. Distinct from the still-deferred FACT-signing require gate (decision:design/fact-signing-enforcement-deferred): facts stay opportunistic (mixed signed/unsigned is normal, live edge strippable); only TICKS take the structural floor, matching the delta-2 "signing is structural from this point forward" posture. The forward-policy "require signing" vertex flag (Gate A) remains a SEPARATE, optional, default-off knob — it governs whether a vertex must sign AT ALL (the first signature, optionally facts), not whether it may stop. Open forward work: the transport era breaks the "key is always local" assumption — see thread:transport-era-signing-key-flow.
high      17:09 [thread] seal-era-boundary-guard: OPEN design question from observation:implementation/seal-no-era-guard-silent-unsigned. sl seal, run in the SIGNED era without keys, silently mints an UNSIGNED tick (exit 0, success output indistinguishable from a signed seal) which breaks chain era-monotonicity (store verify -> CHAIN BROKEN). reanchor already guards this exact boundary and refuses; seal does not. TWO parts to resolve: (1) DISCLOSURE (low-controversy, strictly-more-honest): seal must state its signing outcome — "sealed + signed" vs "sealed UNSIGNED (no key)" — replacing the current byte-identical "tick: project (13 fields)". (2) GUARD (the real call): should seal REFUSE to mint an unsigned tick when prior signed ticks exist (era-aware, parallel to reanchor's refusal and verify's era-monotonicity check), WARN-and-proceed, or allow? Must stay era-aware: a never-signed (pre-era) store sealing unsigned is CORRECT and must not be blocked; only unsigned-AFTER-signed is the violation. Parallels decision:design/fact-signing-enforcement-deferred — same opportunistic-vs-structural tension, but TICKS took the structural posture (delta-2: "signing is structural from this point forward"), so seal arguably SHOULD enforce here even though facts stay opportunistic. Highest-leverage because the SessionEnd hook auto-seals every close — a keys-absent close silently corrupts the chain today. This is the most actionable remaining item in the disclosure pass: part (1) is pure honesty; part (2) closes a real silent-corruption path.
mid       17:09 [observation] implementation/seal-no-era-guard-silent-unsigned: Catalog candidate-bug #2 ("seal mints unsigned tick reporting success; seal never discloses its signing outcome") investigated on keyed vs no-keys copies. BOTH claims CONFIRMED — and this is the ONE REAL finding of the candidate-bug sweep (the HIGH verify-vs-reanchor, FC-04 read-path, F8 ticks-UTF-8, and the reanchor traceback all dissolved / downgraded / fixed). (b) DISCLOSURE: sl seal prints "tick: project (13 fields)" + "stored: seal/..." and NEVER states whether it signed — the output is BYTE-IDENTICAL whether the tick was signed (keyed copy) or not (no-keys copy). The "13 fields" is no signal: the signature COLUMN exists in both, just NULL when unsigned. (a) INTEGRITY (worse than the catalog's "likely harmless artifact"): on a store already in the signed era, sl seal run WITHOUT keys mints an UNSIGNED tick, exit 0, success output — and that unsigned tick BREAKS THE CHAIN: store verify then reports "✗ CHAIN BROKEN ... unsigned tick after signed era — signature stripped or era regressed". Airtight via the symmetric control: the keyed copy's seal minted a SIGNED tick (9/9 signed, chain intact); only the no-keys seal breaks it. ASYMMETRY with reanchor: reanchor GUARDS this exact boundary ("refusing partial re-anchor; a signed fact must not lose authorship") and refuses without keys; seal does NOT — it is the one verb that can silently CREATE the era-regressed / chain-broken state that verify is designed to detect. Contradicts the tick-side STRUCTURAL-signing posture (ticks are vertex-self-signed at a single funnel, "structural from this point forward" — unlike opportunistic per-observer fact signing). REAL-WORLD REACH: the SessionEnd hook runs sl seal automatically on every session close; if keys are ever absent/moved at close (fresh clone pre-keygen, copied store, relocated keydir) the hook silently breaks the chain and nothing says so until a later store verify. Design call held for Kyle — see thread:seal-era-boundary-guard.
tail      17:06 [observation] implementation/read-path-attestation-neutral: FC-04 from observation:design/disclosure-grammar-smoke-test-catalog ("read-path green over broken-signature fact") investigated on a keyed copy. VERDICT: the everyday read/fold path is attestation-NEUTRAL, not attestation-GREEN. Method: tampered a signed fact's payload on a keyed copy. store verify flags it loudly (✗ FACT SIGNATURES BROKEN, names the exact fact: "signature invalid — content does not match the observer's authorship signature"); the read/fold path renders the tampered content verbatim ("message: TAMPERED CONTENT") at every zoom including -vv FULL, with NO attestation glyph — headline identical to a clean fact. The render path is signature-BLIND by construction: lenses/fold.py + commands/fetch.py never inspect per-fact signatures (the only attestation-aware code is the TICK-window/witness-era path used by --ticks; "by-fold signature" in fetch.py is the fold-shape sense, not crypto). So the catalog framing is slightly imprecise: there is no false GREEN — read simply does not speak to attestation at all, UNLIKE store verify's green ✓ which DOES claim ok (that is the real overstatement surface, captured separately as the TIER-1 checkmark fix). CONCLUSION: not a behavioral bug; reframes as a disclosure-DESIGN question — should the everyday read path carry a tamper/unsigned marker, or is attestation-as-a-separate-verb (read = content view, verify = integrity view) the honest separation that keeps crypto out of every read? Same gating as enforcement: with no untrusted receive path yet (decision:design/fact-signing-enforcement-deferred), a read-path tamper-marker has no consumer — it reactivates when something can write facts you did not author. Held for Kyle as a TIER-1 design call, not a fix. Second catalog candidate-bug to dissolve under the same method as the HIGH (observation:implementation/reanchor-verify-not-divergent).

mid       16:19 [thread] error-handling-and-exception-hierarchy: Kyle (2026-06-14): take a deeper look at our exception hierarchy and how we do error handling around it. Triggered by the reanchor bug — operator-facing refusals (resolve_store_path "No store configured", reanchor "requires a .vertex target", engine "no signing key — refusing partial re-anchor", absent .db) are raised as plain ValueError/FileNotFoundError and, with no catch between the _run_* functions and main(), escape as raw tracebacks despite carrying excellent actionable messages. The reanchor fix is LOCALIZED: a catch of (ValueError, FileNotFoundError) at the store view boundary (cli/views/store.py) renders them clean. That is a point patch, not a convention. The systemic questions: (1) should loops have a small exception taxonomy — e.g. an OperatorError/UserError base meaning "expected refusal, render clean + exit nonzero" vs everything else "genuine bug, let it traceback" — rather than catching concrete builtin types per view? (2) where does the catch belong — per-view boundary, the dispatch tiers in cli/app.py, or a single top-level wrapper in main()? (3) the legacy _run_* shims raise and print via painted.show directly while the IR views use ctx.reporter — error rendering is split across both surfaces; unify on the reporter? Hold the earned-granularity line: don't build a hierarchy ahead of need — first audit how many distinct "expected refusal" sites exist across the CLI and whether they cluster.
mid       16:19 [friction] root-pyproject-dep-mirror-gap: The repo ships as a FLAT vendored wheel: root pyproject (strange-loops) bundles every libs/*/src via hatchling and does NOT depend on the workspace members — so root [project].dependencies must mirror the UNION of all vendored libs' third-party deps BY HAND. A dep added to a lib (engine's rfc8785, added with the JCS migration c1f50ed) is invisible to `uv tool install .` until it is also added to root. `uv run --package` masks the gap because it resolves the workspace env, not the flat wheel. SYMPTOM today: `uv tool install . -e --reinstall` uninstalled rfc8785 (it had survived only as a leftover from the 2026-06-12 ceremony's ad-hoc install) → every `sl` command died with "ModuleNotFoundError: No module named 'rfc8785'" at engine import. FIXED: added rfc8785>=0.1.4 to root pyproject with a comment documenting the mirror requirement; sl restored, verified. RESIDUAL (why this stays open): the gap is structural and SILENT — nothing enforces root ⊇ union(libs); the next lib-dep addition reintroduces it, caught only on a fresh tool install. Candidate fixes: (a) a check diffing root deps vs the lib union, wired into ./dev check; (b) make root actually depend on the workspace members instead of vendoring source; (c) dissolve via lib consolidation (thread:lib-consolidation-reconsider — this friction IS the tax). Reinforces the standing anchor that installed-sl is the production path and the workspace-runner form masks staleness.
mid       16:19 [observation] implementation/reanchor-verify-not-divergent: Investigated the smoke-test's HIGH candidate-bug "verify-vs-reanchor opposite verdict on identical bytes" (from observation:design/disclosure-grammar-smoke-test-catalog). VERDICT: not an integrity-verb divergence. Three confirmations on properly-keyed stores: (1) verify and reanchor AGREE on a keyed copy of the current store, and reanchor is BYTE-IDEMPOTENT — the db sha256 is unchanged after "96 facts re-signed, 8 ticks re-chained" because ed25519 is deterministic, so re-signing canonical bytes reproduces identical signatures; (2) reanchor with private keys absent raises BEFORE any write (post-sha == pre-sha) — the engine explicitly guards "refusing partial re-anchor; a signed fact must not lose authorship"; (3) the JCS swap (c1f50ed) is a no-op for existing ASCII/integer payloads — compact-sorted JSON already equals RFC 8785 for that content, which is why reanchor changed zero bytes and why even the pre-JCS archive still verifies chain-intact. The "opposite verdict" reduces to: verify succeeds while reanchor's no-key / no-vertex REFUSAL rendered as a raw Python traceback (uncaught ValueError) — read as a crash / contradicting verdict. Both refusals carry excellent messages; they were just not caught at the CLI boundary. FIX LANDED: catch (ValueError, FileNotFoundError) at the store view boundary (apps/loops/src/loops/cli/views/store.py), render via reporter.err + exit 1; other exception types still raise so genuine bugs stay debuggable. 3 regression tests + full app suite green (1322 passed). This is the first TIER-1 disclosure-honesty fix and it de-risks the broader pass: verify's GREEN is honest about chain-integrity — only the signature-disclosure grammar (checkmark-vs-attested, the backwards warning, covered-vs-signed) still needs work.

high      21:13 [decision] design/fact-signing-enforcement-deferred: Kyle ratified 2026-06-13: DEFER the fact-signing require-on-emit gate AND verify-on-receive to the transport/peer era; make DISCLOSURE honest first. Dissolution reasoning: require-on-emit with no verify-on-receive buys only a locally-complete ledger so verify/disclosure can claim all-post-era-keyed-facts-signed — enforcement in service of disclosure, not of a receiver; no untrusted cross-store receive path exists yet, so build the gate when something is on the other side of it. Counter weighed and overridden for facts: the tick-side delta-2 posture (signing is structural from this point forward) would extend down to facts for a clean-from-here ledger that makes eventual verify-on-receive cheap; rejected now because the clean-ledger benefit is disclosure-facing and achievable instead by honest disclosure of the opportunistic reality, and fact-signing is per-observer/opportunistic vs ticks vertex-self-signed at a single funnel. Net: signing stays opportunistic-on-emit + audit-on-demand (store verify); the require/verify layer reactivates when transport/peer gives verify-on-receive a consumer.
mid       21:04 [observation] implementation/signing-enforcement-status: CODE-CONFIRMED (2026-06-13 smoke-test): fact-signing at emit is OPPORTUNISTIC, not required; verification is AUDIT-ONLY. emit always composes fact_signer_for(path) into the vertex program; a fact signs iff keys/ exists AND the emitting observer has a key (keys/<observer>/ or flat self-key) AND store is in signing era — else appends UNSIGNED silently (no warn, no refusal). NO vertex 'require signature' config exists: the only lang 'strict' flag refuses on emit VALIDATION failures (undeclared kind/observer via validate_emit), NOT on missing signatures. fact_verifier_for/verify_chain are called ONLY in commands/store.py (store verify + reanchor) — operator-invoked, registry-aware (each fact sig checked against its declared observer key exactly). vertex.py receive, program.py, sync.py do NOT verify. Net: sign-if-you-can on write + check-if-you-ask on demand; neither required-on-emit nor verified-on-receive. The progressive-policy + sign-on-emit-verify-on-receive design specified the require+verify layer; it is NOT implemented. NUANCE: require-on-emit is a present gap and the ROOT of the disclosure over-claim (verify renders signed/✓ as an enforced guarantee for an unenforced property). verify-on-receive is correctly DEFERRED not missing — no untrusted cross-store receive path exists yet (local single-writer; verifying your own just-signed fact is circular); load-bearing at the transport/peer era. Kyle's recollection confirmed: the 'vertex must require it' layer is the missing precondition for signing to matter.

tail      19:26 [decision] design/authorship-vs-delegation-layering: Each principal mints their own fact-signing key; delegation is NOT encoded in fact signatures. Kyle's lean, confirmed 2026-06-12 at live keygen (kyle + kyle/loops-claude on project and identity). Rationale: the fact signature makes exactly one claim — authorship of content (identity domain). On-behalf-of is a second claim (authority domain) with its own primitive: act-chains / OBO / endorsements, vouch's L4 territory. Folding delegation into the signature is the write-receipt temptation again — thickening a primitive to carry a claim it cannot make honestly; the carve-out rule says add a separate primitive when the combined claim is live. Forward-compatible: observer name kyle/loops-claude NAMES the delegation by convention today; the future act-chain ATTESTS what the slash only spells — nothing to migrate, layers compose on stable per-principal authorship. Custody honesty: same-machine keys mean organizational not adversarial separation; kyle's signature currently attests 'session that could load kyle's key' until his custody moves to him (vouch custody story).

tail      18:36 [observation] implementation/empty-observer-path-join-footgun: Composition bug caught by delta-2's existing tests on first integration: fact_signer_for resolved keys/<observer>/ via Path join, and observer='' collapses keys_root/'' to the flat layout — an ANONYMOUS writer would have been signed with the vertex key's authorship claim, which is exactly the forgery the per-observer design exists to prevent. Fixed with an explicit guard (empty observer and '..' segments never sign — an observer name is a key, not a path expression). Shape note: the bug class is 'identifier used as path expression'; anywhere observer names hit the filesystem needs the same guard. The break surfaced as a verify failure against the registry — the system's own verification caught the system's own forgery before any human did.

mid       18:19 [decision] design/fact-signing-per-observer-keys: Fact signatures are per-observer authorship claims, Kyle ratified 2026-06-12. Signer callable is (observer, digest) -> sig|None; key layout .loops/keys/<observer>/ed25519.key; verify maps fact.observer -> registry pubkey (the add-observer --key/--keygen registry from delta 2 already IS this mapping). Observers without keys emit unsigned — honest NULL becomes a PER-OBSERVER era, generalizing delta 2's per-store epoch. Layering note: this composes with shipped tick signing rather than replacing it — unsigned-author facts still sit under the vertex-key-signed window hash (custody claim); signed-author facts carry both claims. Custody honesty: on a single machine any local process can read any key in .loops/keys/, so observer separation is organizational not adversarial until keys live with their principals (transport/peer era). Companion mechanism: _fact_row_hash goes era-aware (includes signature only when non-NULL) so signature-stripping breaks the sealed window — delta-2 envelope trick, no re-anchoring of pre-signature rows.
mid       18:17 [decision] design/fact-signature-at-store-column: Fact signature lives as a facts.signature column, NOT a Fact atom field. Kyle ratified 2026-06-12. Rationale: exact delta-2 posture — atoms stay pure, signer injected at store construction, envelope crosses atoms boundary only as read-side view fields. Commitment is content-only: sha256(canonical({kind,ts,payload,observer,origin})), excluding id/rowid — store-assigned identity is custody context, not authored content. This is what makes the signature transport-stable: a receiving store re-derives the commitment from the row and verifies against the observer registry without trusting the sender. Tick chain attests receipt (store-local); fact signature attests authorship (travels). Domain: loops-fact-v1 at the composing layer.

tail      17:54 [decision] practice/reroute-log-sweep-reconcile: ADOPTED 2026-06-12 (Kyle ratified, same conversation as the thread): three-tier capture-and-review. (1) REROUTE LOG — zero-ceremony one-liner into the existing log kind (collect 20) at the moment of routing around anything; no naming/status/fold-key, which is precisely what makes it fire against flow pressure. (2) SWEEP — fast cadence, every session wrap, before the seal: scan session log entries, promote repeat patterns to friction with proper ceremony, update thread statuses, emit the session arc. Name chosen over 'retro' (baggage): the sweep precedes the seal, fits the vocabulary. (3) RECONCILE — slow cadence, own scheduled sessions (weekly-ish): reconcile lens + friction backlog + stale threads + structural fit; promoted to first-class work. Pricing rationale: silent-reroute cost is an externality (local flow saving, global later cost) — fix by making capture cheaper than the reroute, not by discipline. MECHANISM: Stop hook .claude/hooks/turn-capture.py backstops in-the-moment noticing (the thing that demonstrably fails) — fires the capture question once per substantive turn (>=3 tool calls), stop_hook_active-guarded, conversational turns exempt. mid       17:00 [observation] paradigm/rejected-counter-is-state-about-folding: The {target}_rejected counter is a new ontological category in fold state: the first state key the engine writes that no fact supplied and no fold op declared — state ABOUT the folding, not folded state. Same family as Avg's hidden _sum/_count, but those are implementation detail of a declared op; _rejected is the engine commenting on the quality of its own input stream. If this category grows (parse-rejection counts? grant-rejection counts? boundary-misfire counts?), it wants a naming convention and a place in the tick envelope — observability of the fold process itself, which connects directly to robustness-as-visibility-of-failures. Noted, not prescribed; second instance earns the design.
tail      17:00 [friction] add-verb-gap-boundary-and-preview: Extending the signing era today required adding 'boundary when=seal' + a seal kind decl to five vertex files — sl add <v> kind exists and could have done the kind half, but there is NO 'sl add <v> boundary' (or preview) verb, so half the edit had no tool and I hand-rolled a python depth-scanning splice for BOTH halves. Pattern worth naming: a partial verb surface causes total bypass — when the tool covers 50% of a compound edit, the operator does 100% manually and the splice/validate machinery (kdl_splice, parse-before-write) protects nothing. Fix shape: add boundary + preview subcommands to the add verb; they are single-line splices, the library already exists.
tail      17:00 [friction] check-should-read-rule-from-receipt: rebirth --check requires --rule to be re-asserted manually, but the receipt fact already records the transform rule — running --check without it re-runs IDENTITY against a ulid-migration rebirth and reports false mismatches (live scare 2026-06-12, mid fold-determinism validation: rows 6-9 'mismatched' before I realized the rule defaulted). The receipt is the attestation; the verifier asking the operator to restate what the artifact attests is backwards. Fix: --check reads rule from the receipt fact, --rule becomes an override-with-warning. Small, but it is exactly the class of bug the attestation arc exists to prevent — trust the signed claim, not operator memory.

mid       16:35 [decision] design/fold-replay-order-event-time: Two orders, two authorities — the dissolution that resolves the oracle's merge-non-commutativity finding without touching chain-witness-order: FOLD REPLAY orders by (ts, id) — event order, store-independent total order — so merge(A,B) and merge(B,A) re-fold identically; WITNESS ORDER (rowid) remains the chain/window/attestation authority — merge directions ARE different custody events and their chains legitimately differ. Changed sites: SqliteStore.since/since_raw/replay_cursor + latest_by_kind(_where) (ts,id); store_reader facts_by_kind + resolve_entity_id (fixes ref-time rowid-blindness, H4); vertex_reader combined-read sort key (ts,id) — its own NOTE had documented the tie nondeterminism; merge.py INSERT..SELECT ORDER BY ts,id (was unordered scan). Tick/window/chain paths untouched: append_tick, window hashing, _window_facts, FTS cursors all stay rowid. since_raw/replay_cursor now also inject _ts (SELECT gains ts) and Vertex.receive injects _ts on the live path — Latest folds get the same envelope everywhere. Post-rebirth id==event order makes (ts,id) and id-alone agree above ms resolution; (ts,id) chosen because it is also correct for un-reborn mixed-era stores (the H4 general rule). Pinned by TestMergeFoldCommutativity.
tail      16:35 [decision] design/fold-off-type-skip-with-counter: R2 RESOLVED (Kyle, 2026-06-12): an off-type value in a numeric fold (Sum/Avg/Min/Max/TopN-by) is SKIPPED — no state mutation, Avg denominator untouched — and recorded in a deterministic {target}_rejected counter in fold state. Bool is off-type (Python bool-is-int silently folded true as 1). Latest joins the rule: missing _ts rejects, NEVER falls back to time.time() (replay determinism). Missing field stays silent-skip (absence is not an error); off-type presence is. Errors-as-state over errors-as-facts: visible in every snapshot, zero new machinery, no write-on-read, forward-compatible with an error-fact layer later. Chosen over error-fact-at-engine-funnel (heavier, M4-level) and silent-skip-Go-parity (invisible failures contradict robustness=visibility). PROTOCOL-LEVEL: loops-go must implement the same rule + counter; vectors should include bool, numeric-string, and missing-_ts cases. Implemented in atoms/engine.py (_is_number/_reject), pinned by libs/atoms/tests/test_fold_rejection.py.

mid       02:49 [decision] design/rebirth-implementation-shape: rebirth_store lands in libs/store as sibling of slice/merge. Shape: (1) _expected_rows is the shared spine — rebirth writes what it returns, verify_rebirth diffs against it; same function, write then check, so the receipt claim and its verification cannot drift. (2) Genesis tick minted through engine.SqliteStore.append_tick — chain logic single-sourced, prev_row-None path gives window_start='' covering all rows including the receipt; fact_cursor lands on the receipt (seal semantics: attestation covers its own justification). (3) Receipt carries source_content_sha256 (witness-order row hash, the verifiable claim) AND source_file_sha256 (forensic bytes-at-moment) — file hash alone false-alarms under WAL checkpoint/VACUUM. (4) engine exports tick_row_hash publicly: the receipt's chain-head claim uses THE chain's hash function, not a reimplementation. (5) Old tick envelopes re-enter verbatim as tick.<name> facts — old signatures verify against original bytes; old-to-new cursor mapping recomputable from the deterministic transform, never stored. (6) Transforms: identity, ulid-migration (canonical-form rule covering all three id eras), filtered (rule string must describe predicate; verify requires the original Transform). Interleave deferred explicitly — merge-shaped, different arity. CLI: loops store rebirth, signing composed from SOURCE vertex custody (the new incarnation is the lineage's next chapter). mid       02:49 [observation] ops/three-id-eras-in-stores: Live rebirth of project.db surfaced a THIRD id era: 919 lowercase ULIDs (sqlite-ulid C-extension era) alongside 872 uuid4 ids and ~258 canonical python-ulid ids. Lowercase sorts above uppercase in ASCII, so the lowercase era is ALSO order-broken — 01kjtv... sorts after every 01KTQP... forever. The mixed-era story was always told as two eras; the itch was one number reading wrong (1791 ids migrated vs the 872 the story predicted). ulid-migration needs no change: the canonical-form rule (uppercase Crockford or re-mint) covers all three eras uniformly — one rule in the receipt, not three.
mid       02:38 [observation] design/rebirth-ref-rewrite-dissolves: Ref-rewrite component of rebirth dissolves: payload refs are stored entity-keyed (kind:key), resolved to fact ids at READ time (resolve_entity_id), so id migration needs no payload rewriting. Raw old ids appear only in prose messages (32/2048 facts in project.db) — history, not structure; rewriting would falsify quotes. Old tick envelopes re-enter as tick-facts VERBATIM (signature must verify against original bytes); old-to-new id mapping stays recomputable because the migration transform is deterministic: new_id = ULID(ms(fact.ts) || sha256(old_id)[:10]). Determinism is what makes receipt-verification-by-re-run an operation rather than a promise.

mid       22:55 [friction] chain-cursor-assumes-ulid-order: Resolved by design/chain-witness-order: cursor = append edge by rowid, window membership/hash/coverage by rowid range. 28 chain tests incl. TestMixedIdEras regression class reproducing the exact production shape (legacy ticks + uuid4 era + epoch). 782 engine tests pass; production sl store verify clean.
mid       22:55 [decision] design/chain-witness-order: Chain ordering authority is witness order (rowid), never id order. Window cursors stay fact ids (portable handles); membership and hashing resolve cursor->rowid and walk append order. append_tick cursor = id of newest fact BY ROWID, not MAX(id). Fixes mixed-id-era vacuous windows (uuid4 era sorts above all ULIDs, pinning MAX(id) mid-history forever) AND late-arrival false alarms (backfilled fact with honest old event-ts landed inside a sealed id-window = tamper alarm caused by truthfulness; in witness order it lands on live edge, sealed by next tick as received-now). Deliberate semantics flip pinned in tests: backdated-id arrival is no longer a break; displacing a covered row's rowid is. ULID keeps its job — event order for the read path. Already-minted epoch tick still verifies (empty window hashes identically under both orderings). Known interim consequence on mixed stores: project epoch cursor resolves to rowid 1121/2019, so the NEXT tick seals ~900 pre-epoch facts as-of-seal-time — strictly more protection but coverage does not distinguish sealed-since-receipt from sealed-late; rebirth-with-receipt supersedes.
mid       22:48 [observation] design/event-order-vs-witness-order: Two irreducible orders, two claims. Event order (ULID, fact.ts) = when things happened; read-path's order; human-scale, ties meaningless. Witness order (rowid) = when this store received them; the chain's order — chain claims receipt-integrity, not chronology. The killer case is late arrival, not sub-ms ties: a backfilled/synced fact carries an honest old event-ts; under id-ordered windows it lands inside a sealed window and triggers a false tamper alarm caused by truthfulness; under append-ordered windows the next tick covers it honestly. Lamport in system vocabulary: each store is an observer with its own experiential sequence; cross-store order is constructed (merge, with receipt = new observer born), not discovered. ULID was never failing at its job; it was the wrong authority for the chain's claim regardless of tie behavior.
mid       22:26 [friction] chain-cursor-assumes-ulid-order: Tick chain windows are permanently empty in mixed-id-era stores. append_tick uses MAX(id) as fact_cursor and window queries use id-range (WHERE id > ? AND id <= ?), assuming ids are lexicographically append-ordered. True for ULIDs; false for stores with pre-2026-05-17 uuid4 facts (project: 872 uuid4 / 1145 ulid; also identity, comms/native, comms/discord, session). Lowercase-hex uuid4s sort above all ULIDs, so MAX(id) pins to a mid-history uuid4 fact (project: rowid 1121/2017, a March 20 observation) forever — every tick mints window_start == fact_cursor == that uuid4, empty window, window_hash = sha256 of empty input. verify reports chain intact (true) while covering zero facts (vacuous). Found checking why epoch tick reported 0 covered: epoch-empty-window is by design, but the cursor it anchored is wrong, and coverage would never accrue at tick 2. Fresh pure-ULID stores unaffected.

mid       21:45 [decision] design/tick-signature-in-chain-envelope: Kyle's call 2026-06-09 (recommended option): the successor tick's prev_hash commits to its predecessor's SIGNATURE via an era-aware envelope — _tick_row_hash includes a signature key only when the column is non-NULL, so pre-chain and pre-signature rows hash byte-identically to delta 1 (full back-compat, no re-anchoring). Construction: signature signs the 10-field commitment hash (sign-the-content); the row-identity hash that successors chain over includes the signature (chain-over-content+signature) — standard two-hash construction, avoids circularity. Consequence: selective signature-strip breaks the successor's prev_hash and escalates to full-cascade forgery; era-monotonicity rule (unsigned chained tick after a signed one = break) catches the head-strip case. Residual boundary both options share: TOTAL rewrite is indistinguishable from legacy era — anchored only by the registry in the .vertex (outside the store) and future external witnessing; store verify flags declared-key-but-zero-signed-ticks as the cross-artifact tripwire. This fork was the one consequence the evening design session didn't walk.

high      21:08 [decision] design/tick-key-custody-colocated: Ratified: private key lives at .loops/keys/ next to the store it signs — custody co-located, matching delta 1 semantics exactly (slice/merge strip chain → new custody context → key dies with the store's home). Algorithm: Ed25519 (deterministic per RFC 8032 — right property for tamper-evidence; RSA-PSS randomized; JWT layer was wrong shape anyway, detached-digest-signature is a new sign surface either way). Domain-separation prefix loops-tick-v1: baked in from the start. Primitive in libs/sign (new module, load_or_generate pattern). Engine boundary: INJECTION not import — append_tick takes optional signer callable, verify_chain takes optional key-lookup, apps/loops composes; preserves no-cross-lib-imports, makes progressive policy structural (no signer = legacy era), and answers May's vouch lib-boundary question by the same pattern.
mid       21:01 [decision] design/peer-as-exchange-edge-relation: Ratified: Peer keeps the name, retires the framing. The 'convenience bundle: Observer + Grant' header line goes — Peer is the exchange-edge relation: observer (name+key) + exchange policy (Grant) + transport + trust config, minted only when a custody boundary is crossed. Discriminator: if no custody boundary is crossed, nothing is a Peer — local delegation is Observer + Grant directly (delegate() is hierarchy, not peerage). Both senses of 'peer' (networking endpoint, social standing) converge at the edge; the misfit only existed because the old bundle covered local cases too. Rejected alternative: Principal — names the identity (Observer's seat, already taken) not the relation, and imports OAuth frame against vocabulary-as-sibling-layers. Falsifiable prediction that sold it: Peer entries appear only in PAIRS of stores — if vertex A holds a Peer entry for B's observer, B holds one for A's, because exchange is what minted them. A one-sided Peer entry that isn't a half-configured exchange falsifies the vocabulary.

mid       20:32 [observation] design/peer-was-never-the-base-identity: Caught at first real use of the Peer concept (delta 2 signer design): May decisions say 'verify against Peer.key' but engine/peer.py's own header documents Peer as 'convenience bundle: Observer + Grant' — Observer is the base identity primitive and always was (every fact carries an observer string; scripts/services/sources already emit as observers, never dangling at the data layer). The key belongs to the OBSERVER, not Peer: registry is observer-name → public key. Peer re-grounds as relational — an observer seen from the federation edge, bundled with exchange policy (Grant, later transport) — not a kind of entity. Resolves the vertex-as-self-peer strain: the vertex is an observer of its own stream (tick = observation of the window), which is the paradigm being literal. Layering: identity (observer+key) / authorization (Grant) / relationship (Peer). Putting key on Peer would have fused identity with authorization — the fusion grant_of() exists to prevent.
high      20:24 [decision] design/tick-signature-on-every-tick: Delta 2 shape: signature column on EVERY tick row, computed in append_tick over the existing _tick_row_hash (which commits to prev_hash + window_hash, so each signature transitively covers everything behind it). No head-anchor artifact — a separate head record is a mutable pointer wearing an anchor costume (write-receipt principle); the tick IS the commitment shape, the signature belongs on the commitment. Dissolves 'the head' as a special case: every tick self-verifying, head is just the newest. Pre-signature ticks render as era, never retro-claimed — same move as delta 1's chain columns. Cost negligible at session-boundary cadence. Also the rehearsal for delta 3 (Fact.signature): same pattern one layer up, proven first where rows number ~200 not ~2000. Kyle's framing sharpened it: the decision is 'signing is structural from this point forward', not 'patch the head'. External witnessing (publish head hash outside the store) noted as a complement, not an alternative — not this delta.

mid       19:39 [decision] design/tick-chain-at-store-layer: Tick hash-chaining lives at the STORE layer, not the Tick atom (Kyle's call 2026-06-09, recommended option). Three columns on ticks table: prev_hash (sha256 of previous tick row's canonical bytes — chains the sequence), fact_cursor (max fact ULID at tick time — explicit id-based window boundary, not ts-inferred), window_hash (sha256 over canonical fact rows in (prev_cursor, cursor] in id order — makes FACTS tamper-evident, the actual prize). Rationale: a chain is a property of the persisted sequence, not the snapshot; Tick atom stays pure, no API/serialization change; merge honestly breaks chains (new custody context = correct semantics). Dissolution: delta 1 of the provenance arc requires NO substrate/atom change — pure store-layer property. Precedents followed: pre-chain rows stay NULL (era marker, uuid4-wedge posture); first chained tick's window starts at migration-time max id (epoch marker, no false coverage claims); canonicalization = sorted-compact JSON in one documented helper, NOT JCS — chain needs determinism not interop; JCS stays pinned for federation-facing manifests (delta 2+). Verification walks ticks recomputing both hashes; facts after last tick are the honest uncovered live edge.

high      19:10 [thread] vouch-evidence-layer-collapse: Dissolution analysis (2026-06-09, Kyle's question): does enterprise vouch collapse back into loops-native? Answer: the EVIDENCE layer collapses almost entirely — signed facts (sign lib), authenticated emission (Peer), audience scoping (Grant at read/transport), manifest+completion as opening/closing receipt facts, tamper-evident archive as hash-chained ticks. The ENFORCEMENT layer does not: verifier gate (refusal-before-effect), foreign-artifact canonicalization, revocation — all land in the carve-out class write-receipt-vs-temporal-query already drew (gate joins CAS/vote/claim/lease). Strongest-form dissolution: boundary lands where an existing principle already drew it. Bidirectional repair: vouch converts loops' custodial trust (immutability by convention, observer-as-string, merge-by-politeness) to cryptographic; loops gives Peer/Grant/sign their first consumer internally. Concrete deltas if pursued: (1) signature field on Fact via sign lib, (2) emit-through-Peer path, (3) tick hash-chaining, (4) Grant-scoped read/transport. Each is hardening an existing property, not a new subsystem.

mid       03:20 [thread] python-bugs-from-go-oracle: Fix-BOTH bugs the loops-go oracle surfaced LIVE in this monorepo Python (libs/atoms, libs/engine) — our code has them too, actionable here independent of the loops-go protocol forks. mid       18:40 [decision] design/signature-vs-body-resolved-by-binding-level: Decision (resolves the open question in three-layer-auth-composition): signature-proves-emission vs signature-proves-responsibility was a false dichotomy — they are different LEVELS, not competitors. Fact.signature over a compiled manifest = binds execution (L4); BODY act-chain (act=alice) = attributes responsibility (RFC8693 act-claim shape, L1-ish provenance). Both coexist: signature governs what executes, act-chain attributes who is responsible. Two independent derivations converged on this — the binding-target-spectrum (agent-attestation vertex) and the MSFT-Entra grounding (agent-id distinct from principal-signature). High confidence.
mid       18:40 [decision] design/vouch-act-side-libssign-plus-l4: Decision: vouch act-side = libs/sign canonical-bytes primitive + an L4 binding discipline. Answers the owed libs/sign-primitive-surface question. libs/sign signs canonical bytes (consumable by loops-engine AND Java, no loops deps); the L4 discipline is that those bytes ARE a compiled byte-deterministic execution artifact — not a scope/claim. Governance = byte-equality, no LLM between sign and execute. Wire = base Transaction Tokens (WG draft) carrying the manifest hash; vouch differentiates from the individual txtokens-for-agents draft, which binds tctx params not execution. Full landscape derivation + 4-level binding-target-spectrum lives in the agent-attestation vertex (sl read agent-attestation).

mid       17:20 [decision] paradigm/audience-distinct-from-authorization: Who is allowed to RECEIVE what a service emits is a different question from who is allowed to ACT against that service. Collapsing both into 'authorization' loses the distinction. The agent-as-compiler model closes act-side cleanly (signature binds exact payload, infra replays signed manifest, agent never holds active credential). It does NOT close receive-side: during discovery phase the agent reads via authorized API calls and the output flows into LLM context — if agent is compromised mid-discovery, the data exfiltration vector is open even though no write-side authorization is violated. Surfaced via Gemini exchange 2026-05-20 where Gemini wallpapered the read-side exfiltration gap with 'don't grant raw DB access' (true but evasive — API-mediated reads still leak whatever the API returns). Maps onto Phase 1 vocab walk — 'audience' was one of the four words still to walk (alongside principal, rescission, transport). This is the audience axis: act-side = who can invoke; receive-side = who can be told. Vouch design must address both, not conflate. Implication for libs/sign + libs/vouch: signature on an emission proves provenance (act-side); audience-scoping on a fact's visibility is a separate primitive (receive-side) that probably belongs in engine emit/receive flow rather than libs/sign. Discriminator for future design: when a vouch question lands, ask 'is this about who can act or who can receive?' before choosing primitives.
mid       17:20 [thread] vouch-oauth-integration-question: Does vouch (identity exchange / signing layer) integrate INTO existing enterprise OAuth servers (Keycloak/Okta/Auth0/Ping/Hydra) or stand alone? Raised first by Kyle's architect during initial sketch of the overall concept; resurfaced 2026-05-20 via Gemini exchange from the deployment-pattern angle. Recurring question deserves its own handle. Working answer (Gemini at deployment layer, probably right): identity/exchange/keys live IN existing OAuth server via RFC 8693 token-exchange extension; the registry/policy/state layer stays separate. Maps onto our libs/sign + libs/vouch split — libs/sign as primitive any OAuth server could host; libs/vouch as federation-path layer that doesn't need to live there. Open: at loops substrate layer where we actually work, does this change anything? Probably not directly — libs/sign and libs/vouch are repo libs, not deployment artifacts. But it shapes the deployment story: 'where does homelab IdP host this' and 'where does enterprise host this' have the same answer (existing OAuth server for identity, separate service for policy/registry). Resolves when: deployment-layer story written + relationship between libs/sign + libs/vouch + existing OAuth servers articulated. Sits alongside vouch-deployment-substrate-constraint — same question viewed from different angle (OAuth-side vs java-service-side).
high      17:19 [decision] paradigm/agent-as-compiler-not-operator: Agent compiles an immutable execution manifest; human signs the manifest; infrastructure executes — agent is courier, never operator. The signed thing IS the compiled intent, not a capability grant. Reframes vouch flow: discovery (low-risk broad read) → compile (agent produces deterministic payload) → attestation (peer signs exact payload) → execution (infra replays signed payload). Surfaced via Gemini exchange 2026-05-20; Kyle pulled it out as the load-bearing reframe. Maps onto sign-on-emit/verify-on-receive: the 'execution manifest' IS a Fact with specific kind; signature IS the attestation; execution boundary triggers on attested-fact existence in scope. Reframes multi-endpoint problem — target service doesn't expose N privileged endpoints to untrusted agents; it exposes a single 'execute-attested-fact' boundary that reads payload from the signed fact body. This is the loops-paradigm answer to the enterprise-IAM Registry pattern: facts → boundary → execution, with attestation as the gate. Industry drafts (Prakash/AIP) building inline runtime proxies with regex filters get dissolved by this framing — once the agent is a compiler not an operator, there's nothing on the wire to babysit. The threat surface compresses to (a) discovery-phase read exfiltration, still open, and (b) compile-time argument injection between human-review and infrastructure-execution, closed by signature-binds-exact-payload.

tail      02:32 [observation] pattern/auto-resolver-coherent-until-trace-split-it: Timeline grounding 2026-05-19: the auto-resolver was internally coherent from 2026-03-09 (39d8de9) introduction through 2026-05-15. Slash-form on both write (_resolve_entity_refs) and read (no walker existed yet — _ref siblings WERE the navigation mechanism). The convention split was created in 2026-05-16 by the trace verb commit (803ba03) — cross-kind ref walking needed unambiguous parsing, chose colon over slash, fixed the read parser (_parse_fact_refs introduced as colon-only), did not propagate to write side. Same commit message explicitly notes catching 'ref parser used / separator instead of : (refs are kind:key)' — the team thought the bug was caught when only the read side was fixed. Reframes 'messy codebase' as 'deferred-completion debt from a 3-day-old multi-step refactor.' This is a normal failure mode of substantial refactors (sweep gap), not a discipline collapse. Useful as orienting context whenever the typed-refs work is picked up — the convention drift has a specific origin commit and a specific deferred sweep, not ambient cruft.
tail      02:32 [observation] architecture/slash-overload-as-system-notation-gap: At least six distinct conceptual meanings on / in the codebase: (1) kind/key entity address (CLI input), (2) kind/key payload value scanned by auto-resolver, (3) namespace/topic fold-key prefix (today's bug site), (4) parent/scope observer hierarchy (engine/observer.py), (5) template/subdir vertex template (init.py), (6) parent/alias combine child (resolve.py:_resolve_vertex_for_dispatch). Each consumer chose / organically because it's the obvious separator; the collision came from accumulation not design. Filesystem solved this with one meaning (hierarchy); URIs solved it with reserved chars per role (scheme: path/ ?query #fragment). Loops drifted into multi-meaning slash without picking either strategy. The non-decision IS the structural gap — not the resolver's behavior specifically, but the absence of a chosen notation methodology. Adjacent to but distinct from typed-refs question: even with typed addresses, the / character still does five other things in the codebase that occasionally collide.
mid       02:32 [thread] typed-refs-redesign: Entry point for next session. Central question: should refs become a typed dataclass (Ref(kind, key)) at the substrate layer rather than a parsed-string convention? Evidence accumulated 2026-05-19 session: convention drift between write-side (slash) and read-side (colon) created May-16 by the trace verb commit and not propagated; the auto-resolver pattern-scans payload values producing the heuristic-eats-semantic-field bug class (cite ref-stealing, today's topic-as-ref, others); vestigial _ref siblings written by resolver, read by zero production code. Calibration warning attached: this was a single-arc conviction that felt structural at the time of emission. Confirming evidence bar before promoting to decision: at least one cross-arc encounter (next bug instance, next ref-touching commit) where the typed-ref framing either lands cleanly or surfaces friction. Adjacent questions parked: slash-overload-taxonomy thread, whether _parse_fact_refs should accept slash-form as back-compat, what wire form serialization settles on. Closes when: typed-refs is implemented OR rejected OR clearly deferred behind a more urgent forcing function.
mid       02:32 [decision] design/park-may-16-write-side-migration-pending-typed-ref-question: 2026-05-19 session close: do NOT propagate colon convention through the write-side resolver to complete the May-16 trace migration. The migration is real and the gap is real, but the right shape depends on whether refs become typed (hypothesis:refs-as-typed-address-dataclass). If typed, the colon-vs-slash choice becomes arbitrary at the serialization boundary and only one of the two paths needs to be supported as the canonical wire form. If we propagate colon now, then later land typed-refs, we'll have done convention-migration work twice. Cost of waiting: today's fold-key skip (commit 33937f6) stays as cosmetic workaround for one symptom; receipt continues to miscount canonical refs. Acceptable for one decision-cycle. Reversal trigger: a) typed-refs lands and chooses a wire form, or b) typed-refs is rejected as a design direction (then propagate colon as originally scoped).
high      02:32 [hypothesis] refs-as-typed-address-dataclass: The whole class of bugs we surfaced this session (today's fold-key skip, write/read convention drift, pattern-scan-as-inference, false-positive WARNs, vestigial _ref siblings consuming nothing) dissolves into one structural move: Ref(kind: str, key: str) as a typed dataclass. Characters at the serialization boundary become arbitrary; the in-memory shape is unambiguous; resolver/walker/writer all operate on typed pairs. Confirming evidence bar: implement on a bounded slice (the resolver + _parse_fact_refs as the two ends of the convention drift), measure (a) LOC reduction, (b) elimination of slash-overload-class bugs across resolver, walker, lens code, (c) test surface simplification. The pull is structural and feels right at evidence-N=1; the discipline says proposed not confirmed until cross-arc evidence.

high      21:10 [thread] stdin-message-for-emit: Design landed: explicit flags --stdin FIELD + --file FIELD=PATH (see decision:design/emit-stdin-file-as-call-site-convention). mid       21:10 [decision] design/emit-stdin-file-as-call-site-convention: Stdin/file expansion for emit ships as explicit flags: --stdin FIELD (read sys.stdin into named field, TTY-guarded, single trailing newline stripped) and --file FIELD=PATH (action=append for multiples, ~ expanded, single trailing newline stripped). NOT inline magic syntax (=- / =@path) and NOT per-kind declaration (no prose_fields on LoopDef). Rationale: (1) Layer separation — the feature is call-site-semantic (user decides per invocation), not kind-semantic (vertex author decides per kind), so it does not belong in vertex declarations. See observation:pattern/declaration-vs-call-site-discriminator. (2) Inline magic syntax collides with legitimate @-bearing values — verified empirically that topic=foo@example.com and topic=https://user:pass@host/path store literally today. The @@ escape tax would apply to every email/URL going forward. Not vanishing-rare. (3) Explicit flags match loops house style (--strict, --quiet, --dry-run, --observer) — explicit-over-implicit. Three pivots arrived here: hardcode message= → declaration-driven via prose_fields → universal magic syntax → explicit flags. Each pivot dissolved more structure; final form has ZERO ast/loader/engine/atoms/vertex-file changes. Pure CLI-layer feature, ~40 LOC helper + ~80 LOC tests. Error model: multiple --stdin → error (one stdin source); --stdin with TTY → error; --file with nonexistent path → error; field appears both in parts AND via --stdin/--file → error (conflicting sources, ambiguous intent).
mid       21:10 [observation] practice/empirical-precheck-collapses-design-pivots: Three pivots in one session designing stdin/file expansion for emit (hardcode message= → declaration-driven via prose_fields → universal magic syntax via =- and =@ → explicit --stdin and --file flags). Each pivot toward less structure, each labeled "truly dissolved plan." The cascade itself was aesthetic capture — recursion-pull-resistible-via-pre-check was in the growing-edge but I missed firing it. The trivial empirical check that would have collapsed three pivots into one: "sl emit project decision topic=foo@example.com --dry-run" takes 2 seconds and would have shown the @ collision immediately, surfacing explicit-flags as the answer at pivot 1. Curl-convention vibes anchored me three pivots deep; one shell command would have grounded it. SHARPENING for future-me: when about to write up a design that depends on syntactic assumptions about real values, RUN the assumption against real data first — before the design writeup, not after. Adjacent to but sharper than recursion-pull-resistible-via-pre-check: that pattern is about aesthetic-driven artifacts; THIS is about design-frame anchoring on inherited conventions.
mid       21:09 [observation] pattern/loops-field-role-family: search and preview are a real family on LoopDef: "a list of payload field names with a particular role." Differ only in which consumer reads them and on which side of the lifecycle (write-side indexing vs read-side rendering). fold/boundary/parse are a different family — runtime semantics, not field-role metadata. Family membership criterion: per-kind variability (each kind declares its own answer). prose-as-stdin-eligibility was almost the third member but failed the criterion — call-site-semantic, not kind-semantic. N=2 confirmed members; family observation kept as substrate for recognizing future candidates. Do NOT refactor to unified fields{} block or per-field-type system yet — patterns earn their refactor through use-forced shared shape, not aesthetic.
mid       21:09 [observation] pattern/declaration-vs-call-site-discriminator: Discriminator for "declare per-kind on the loop block" vs "universal CLI feature": does each consumer of the field-role need per-kind variability? preview YES (friction:status+message, decision:message, change:empty — visible heterogeneity). search YES (different kinds index different fields). prose-as-stdin-eligibility NO — the kind does not decide; the user at the call site does, by writing the flag at emit time. Kind-semantic properties earn declarations; call-site conventions do not. Surfaced 2026-05-19 designing stdin/file expansion for emit. The aesthetic parallel to preview_fields was structurally superficial — looked like a sibling, turned out to be a different layer (input convention vs render selection). Future-me: when proposing a new loop-block declaration, ask this discriminator first.

mid       13:51 [decision] design/lenses-consume-declared-properties: Lenses consume declared properties of kinds. They do not inspect data shape to make rendering decisions. Properties of kinds (preview fields, field semantics like state-vs-accumulate, salience hints) are declared in the .vertex spec, threaded through atoms (FoldSection, FoldItem), and consumed by lenses. Zoom and width are user-controlled (-q/-v/-vv, terminal vs piped) — not lens-derived. RATIONALE: Auto-zoom (commits c5c2cbc + 7c3bca6, reverted in ad232622ab88ccf7ac85014dbf81e9fff7afa9ab) inverted this — the lens read len(items) and key-namespace structure at render time and chose its own fidelity. One session produced two frictions and one escape-hatch flag (--facts). The pattern was generating override flags as fast as it generated smart defaults. PROTOTYPE: Per-kind preview (commit 02ee436) is the correct shape — 'preview "field" "field"' declared in the loop block, parsed into LoopDef.preview_fields, threaded through FoldSection.preview_fields (atoms), consumed in fold.py's body-rendering branch. Spec → atom → lens. IMPLICATIONS: (1) Cardinality auto-zoom is rejected as a lens responsibility — if users want different fidelity by kind, declare it via existing -q/-v/-vv or per-kind properties. (2) The diff/refs strip (commit 2621be9 trace.py) is a dissolution candidate — refs are accumulate-not-state, which is a property of the field that should be declared on the atom and consumed by trace.py + any other consumer, not hardcoded locally. (3) The preview-ls asymmetry (ls --kind doesn't surface preview_fields even though the spec declares it) is the next mechanical fix — completes the spec-to-introspection thread. TEST FOR THE MOMENT: when proposing a rendering improvement, ask 'does this consume a declared property of the kind, or does it inspect data shape?' If the latter, the answer belongs in the spec, not the lens.
mid       13:14 [friction] thread-namespace-breakdown-degenerate: When --kind has ≥2 namespace prefixes but ungrouped >> grouped, MINIMAL still renders the namespace breakdown rather than falling back to the key list. Concrete: 'sl read project --kind thread' shows 'autoresearch/ (1)  substrate-friction/ (1)  (ungrouped: 173)' — the partition surfaces ~1% of items and hides the actual 173-entry index. Spec's '≥2 groups → namespace breakdown' is the trigger; missing condition is a ratio check (e.g. if ungrouped > 2 * sum(grouped), fall back to key list). Friction tier: low — workaround is --facts. Worth fixing for honesty of the MINIMAL render.

mid       02:11 [friction] auto-zoom-MINIMAL-degenerate-on-flat-keys: RESOLVED 2026-05-18 (commit 7c3bca6). _render_section_minimal rewritten as two-branch: namespace breakdown when ≥2 groups, key-list fallback otherwise. Smoke confirmed on real project store — paradigm/ (26) now lists 26 keys with prefix stripped, cite (32 flat keys) now lists 32 contexts, design/ (187) lists 187 keys, root firehose still shows the multi-namespace breakdown. 1270 tests pass. Pattern recurring: when fixing a buggy spec, scan tests for assertions locking the bug.
mid       02:11 [decision] rendering/facts-disables-auto-zoom: --facts joins -q/-v/-vv as a loudness signal that disables auto-zoom. Rationale: --facts requests MORE per item (compression history, fact lineage, n counts); auto-zoom-DOWN to MINIMAL renders LESS (or nothing) per item. Direct contradiction — orthogonal-in-spec, anti-orthogonal-in-effect. --refs/--plain/--json remain truly orthogonal (visibility/format, not loudness). The classification: explicit content-requesting flags disable auto-zoom-DOWN. Patch at apps/loops/src/loops/cli/views/fold.py — auto_zoom gate adds 'and not args.facts'. Anchored by friction:auto-zoom-neutralizes-facts-flag.
mid       02:11 [decision] rendering/minimal-as-honest-index: MINIMAL renders the index ('what's in here?') at different cardinality regimes via two branches: (1) namespace breakdown when keys span ≥2 groups (root firehose orientation: 'design/ (187) architecture/ (82) ...'); (2) one-label-per-line key list otherwise (single-namespace post-narrowing OR flat-key kinds like cite). For by-fold key lists, shared namespace prefix is stripped to match SUMMARY-mode grouped rendering. For collect-fold, label is _first_field(payload). The prior renderer was one-trick (breakdown only) and returned Block.empty in degenerate cases — three real failures: 'X/ (N)' tautology after --key narrowing, blank section on flat-key kinds (cite), and silent loss on single-namespace floods. The two-branch shape preserves the firehose property while making degenerate cases honest. Anchored by friction:auto-zoom-MINIMAL-degenerate-on-flat-keys + advisor reframe from gate-fix to renderer-fix (third pass).
